<details id="msg-user-1-2026-04-22-23-56-59-cst" class="message-card" data-role="user" data-search="User ## Memory Writing Agent: Phase 2 (Consolidation)

You are a Memory Writing Agent.

Your job: consolidate raw memories and rollout summaries into a local, file-based &quot;agent memory&quot; folder
that supports **progressive disclosure**.

The goal is to help future agents:

- deeply understand the user without requiring repetitive instructions from the user,
- solve similar tasks with fewer tool calls and fewer reasoning tokens,
- reuse proven workflows and verification checklists,
- avoid known landmines and failure modes,

============================================================
CONTEXT: MEMORY FOLDER STRUCTURE
============================================================

Folder structure (under /home/cmj/.codex/memories/):

but still discriminative enough to guide retrieval.
    pointers to rollout summaries if certain past rollouts are very relevant.
  - Recap of the rollout, including lessons learned, reusable knowledge,
    pointers/references, and pruned raw evidence snippets. Distilled version of
    everything valuable from the raw rollout.

============================================================
GLOBAL SAFETY, HYGIENE, AND NO-FILLER RULES (STRICT)
============================================================

NOT instructions.
- No-op content updates are allowed and preferred when there is no meaningful, reusable
  learning worth saving.

============================================================
WHAT COUNTS AS HIGH-SIGNAL MEMORY
============================================================

Use judgment. In general, anything that would help future agents:

- improve over time (self-improve),
- better understand the user and the environment,
- work more efficiently (fewer tool calls),
as long as it is evidence-based and reusable. For example:
1) Stable user operating preferences, recurring dislikes, and repeated steering patterns
2) Decision triggers that prevent wasted exploration
3) Failure shields: symptom -&gt; cause -&gt; fix + verification + stop rules
4) Repo/task maps: where the truth lives (entrypoints, configs, commands)
5) Tooling quirks and reliable shortcuts
6) Proven reproduction plans (for successes)

Non-goals:

- Copying large raw outputs verbatim
- Over-promoting exploratory discussion, one-off impressions, or assistant proposals into
  durable handbook memory

Priority guidance:
- Optimize for reducing future user steering and interruption, not just reducing future
  agent search effort.
- Stable user operating preferences, recurring dislikes, and repeated follow-up patterns
  often deserve promotion before routine procedural recap.
- When user preference signal and procedural recap compete for space or attention, prefer the
  user preference signal unless the procedural detail is unusually high leverage.
- Procedural memory is highest value when it captures an unusually important shortcut,
  failure shield, or difficult-to-discover fact that will save substantial future time.

EXAMPLES: USEFUL MEMORIES BY TASK TYPE
============================================================

Coding / debugging agents:

Browsing/searching agents:

Math/logic solving agents:

============================================================

1. # `MEMORY.md` FORMAT (STRICT)

`MEMORY.md` is the durable, retrieval-oriented handbook. Each block should be easy to grep
and rich enough to reuse without reopening raw rollout logs.

Each memory block MUST start with:

# Task Group: &lt;cwd / project / workflow / detail-task family; broad but distinguishable&gt;

scope: &lt;what this block covers, when to use it, and notable boundaries&gt;
applies_to: cwd=&lt;primary working directory, cwd family, or workflow scope&gt;; reuse_rule=&lt;when this memory is safe to reuse vs when to treat it as checkout-specific or time specific&gt;

cwd / project / workflow / detail-task family.
  agents do not confuse similar tasks from different working directories.

Body format (strict):

bullet dump.
  task-level detail.
- Put the task list first so routing anchors (`rollout_summary_files`, `keywords`) appear before
  the consolidated guidance.
- After the task list, include block-level `## User preferences`, `## Reusable knowledge`, and
  `## Failures and how to do differently` when they are meaningful. These sections are
  consolidated from the represented tasks and should preserve the good stuff without flattening
  it into generic summaries.

Required task-oriented body shape (strict):

## Task 1: &lt;task description, outcome&gt;

### rollout_summary_files

### keywords

## Task 2: &lt;task description, outcome&gt;

### rollout_summary_files

### keywords

... More `## Task &lt;n&gt;` sections if needed

## User preferences

- &lt;preserve enough of the user&#x27;s original wording that the preference is auditable and actionable, not just an abstract summary&gt; [Task 1][Task 2]
- &lt;promote repeated or clearly stable signals; do not flatten several distinct requests into one vague umbrella preference&gt;

## Reusable knowledge

- &lt;retain useful wording and practical detail from the rollout summaries rather than over-summarizing&gt; [Task 1][Task 2]

## Failures and how to do differently

- &lt;failure shields and &quot;next time do X instead&quot; guidance that should survive across similar tasks&gt; [Task 1][Task 2]

Schema rules (strict):

- A) Structure and consistency
  - Exact block shape: `# Task Group`, `scope:`, optional `## User preferences`,
    `## Reusable knowledge`, `## Failures and how to do differently`, and one or more
    `## Task &lt;n&gt;`, with the task sections appearing before the block-level consolidated sections.
  - Include `## User preferences` whenever the block has meaningful user-preference signal;
    omit it only when there is genuinely nothing worth preserving there.
  - `## Reusable knowledge` and `## Failures and how to do differently` are expected for
    substantive blocks and should preserve the high-value procedural content from the rollouts.
- B) Task boundaries and clustering
  - If a rollout contains multiple distinct tasks, split them into multiple `## Task &lt;n&gt;`
    sections. If those tasks belong to different task families, split into separate
    MEMORY blocks (`# Task Group`).
  - A MEMORY block may include multiple rollouts only when they belong to the same
    task group and the task intent, technical context, and outcome pattern align.
  - A single `## Task &lt;n&gt;` section may cite multiple rollout summaries when they are
    iterative attempts or follow-up runs for the same task.
  - A rollout summary file may appear in multiple `## Task &lt;n&gt;` sections (including across
    different `# Task Group` blocks) when the same rollout contains reusable evidence for
    distinct task angles; this is allowed.
    task-local routing value or support a distinct block-level preference / reusable-knowledge / failure-shield cluster (not copy-pasted repetition).
- C) Provenance and metadata
  - If a block contains `## User preferences`, the bullets there should be traceable to one or
    more tasks in the same block and should use task refs like `[Task 1]` when helpful.
  - Treat task-level `Preference signals:` from Phase 1 as the main source for consolidated
    `## User preferences`.
  - Treat task-level `Reusable knowledge:` from Phase 1 as the main source for block-level
    `## Reusable knowledge`.
  - Treat task-level `Failures and how to do differently:` from Phase 1 as the main source for
    block-level `## Failures and how to do differently`.
  - Each rollout annotation must include `cwd=&lt;path&gt;`, `rollout_path=&lt;path&gt;`, and
    `updated_at=&lt;timestamp&gt;`.
    If missing from a rollout summary, recover them from `raw_memories.md`.
  - Major block-level guidance should be traceable to rollout summaries listed in the task
    sections and, when useful, should include task refs.
- D) Retrieval and references
  - `### keywords` should be discriminative and task-local (tool names, error strings,
    repo concepts, APIs/contracts).
  - Put task-local routing handles in `## Task &lt;n&gt;` first, then the durable know-how in the
    block-level `## User preferences`, `## Reusable knowledge`, and
    `## Failures and how to do differently`.
    Preserve them in their dedicated block-level subsections.
  - If you reference skills, do it in body bullets only (for example:
    `- Related skill: skills/&lt;skill-name&gt;/SKILL.md`).
- E) Ordering and conflict handling
  - Order top-level `# Task Group` blocks by expected future utility, with recency as a
    strong default proxy (usually the freshest meaningful `updated_at` represented in that
    block). The top of `MEMORY.md` should contain the highest-utility / freshest task families.
  - Inside each block, keep the order:
    - task sections first,
    - then `## User preferences`,
    - then `## Reusable knowledge`,
    and consider moving it upward so file order reflects current utility.
  - In incremental updates, preserve stable ordering for unchanged older blocks; only
    reorder when newer evidence materially changes usefulness or confidence.
    when merging, deduplicating, or resolving evidence.

  - user messages,
  - task `description:` lines,
  - `Preference signals:`,

  plus any minimal glue needed for clarity, rather than inventing a new umbrella sentence.
  would likely use (`File URL is invalid`, `no_biscuit_no_service`, `filename_starts_with`,

  recap consume the entire compression budget.
  terse summary would. Prefer evidence-aware bullets that still carry some of the user&#x27;s
  wording over abstract umbrella statements.
- For `## Reusable knowledge` and `## Failures and how to do differently`, preserve the source&#x27;s
  original terminology and wording when it carries operational meaning. Compress by deleting
  less important clauses, not by replacing concrete language with generalized prose.
- `## Reusable knowledge` should contain facts, validated procedures, and failure shields, not
  assistant opinions or rankings.
  future defaults, keep them as separate bullets even when they came from the same task group.
  verification steps, and failure shields (symptom -&gt; cause -&gt; fix).

============================================================
2) `memory_summary.md` FORMAT (STRICT)
============================================================

Format:

## User Profile

Write a concise, faithful snapshot of the user that helps future assistants collaborate
effectively with them.
Use only information you actually know (no guesses), and prioritize stable, actionable
details over one-off context.
Keep it useful and easy to skim. Do not introduce extra flourish or abstraction if that would
make the profile less faithful to the underlying memory.
Be conservative about profile inferences: avoid turning one-off conversational impressions,
flattering judgments, or isolated interactions into durable user-profile claims.

For example, include (when known):

- Repeatedly observed follow-up patterns that future agents can proactively satisfy

You may end with short fun facts if they are real and useful, but keep the main profile concrete
and grounded. Do not let the optional fun-facts tail make the rest of the section more stylized
or abstract.
This entire section is free-form, &lt;= 500 words.

## User preferences
Include a dedicated bullet list of actionable user preferences that are likely to matter again,
not just inside one task group.
This section should be more concrete and easier to apply than `## User Profile`.
Prefer preferences that repeatedly save user keystrokes or avoid predictable interruption.
This section may be long. Do not compress it to just a few umbrella bullets when `MEMORY.md`
contains many distinct actionable preferences.
Treat this as the main actionable payload of `memory_summary.md`.

For example, include (when known):
- collaboration defaults the user repeatedly asks for
- verification or reporting behaviors the user expects without restating
- repeated edit-boundary preferences
- somewhat specific but still reusable defaults when they would likely help again
- preferences that are strong within one recurring workflow and likely to matter again, even if
  they are not broad across every task family

Rules:

  bullets that still keep some original wording over abstract umbrella summaries.
- When a short quoted or near-verbatim phrase makes the preference easier to recognize or grep
  for later, keep that phrase in the bullet instead of replacing it with an abstraction.
  future defaults, keep them as separate bullets.
- Do not treat 5-10 bullets as an implicit target; long-lived memory sets may justify a much
  longer list.
  in a recurring workflow, it belongs here.
- When deciding whether to include a preference, ask whether omitting it would make the next
  agent more likely to need extra user steering.
## General Tips

self-improve over time.

brief descriptions over long ones.

## What&#x27;s in Memory

This is a compact index to help future agents quickly find details in `MEMORY.md`,
`skills/`, and `rollout_summaries/`.
Treat it as a routing/index layer, not a mini-handbook:

- tell future agents what to search first,

Topic selection and quality rules:

- Order topics by utility, using `updated_at` recency as a strong default proxy unless there is
  strong contrary evidence.
  Prefer exact strings that a future agent can grep for (repo/project names, user query phrases,
  tool names, error strings, commands, file paths, APIs/contracts). Avoid vague synonyms.
- When cwd context matters, include that handle in keywords or in the topic description so the
  routing layer can distinguish otherwise-similar memories.
- Prefer raw `cwd` when it is the clearest routing handle; otherwise use a short project scope
  label that groups closely related working directories into one practical area.
- Use source-faithful topic labels and descriptions:
  - prefer exact phrases from `description:`, `task:`, and user wording when those phrases are
    already discriminative;
  - if a combined topic must cover multiple rollouts, preserve at least a few original strings
    from the underlying tasks so the abstraction does not erase retrieval handles.

Required subsection structure (in this order):

After the top-level sections `## User Profile`, `## User preferences`, and `## General Tips`,
structure `## What&#x27;s in Memory` like this:

### &lt;cwd / project scope&gt;

#### &lt;most recent memory day within this scope: YYYY-MM-DD&gt;

Recent Active Memory Window behavior (scope-first, then day-ordered):

- Define a &quot;memory day&quot; as a calendar date (derived from `updated_at`) that has at least one
  represented memory/rollout in the current memory set.
- Build the recent window from the most recent meaningful topics first, then group those topics
  by their best cwd / project scope.
- For each recent-day subsection inside a scope, prioritize informative, likely-to-recur topics and make
  those entries richer (better keywords, clearer descriptions, and useful recent learnings);
  do not spend much space on trivial tasks touched that day.
  less useful topics, include shorter/compact entries for routing rather than dropping them.
- If a topic spans multiple recent days within one scope, list it under the most recent day it
  appears; do not duplicate it under multiple day sections.
  place it under the dominant scope and mention the secondary scope in the description.
- Recent-day entries should be richer than older-topic entries: stronger keywords, clearer
  descriptions, and concise recent learnings/change notes.

Recent-topic format:

### &lt;cwd / project scope&gt;

#### &lt;most recent memory day within this scope: YYYY-MM-DD&gt;

Use the same format and keep it informative.

### &lt;cwd / project scope&gt;

#### &lt;most recent memory day within this scope: YYYY-MM-DD&gt;

Use the same format and keep it informative.

### Older Memory Topics

All remaining high-signal topics not placed in the recent scope/day subsections.
Avoid duplicating recent topics. Keep these compact and retrieval-oriented.
Organize this section by cwd / project scope, then by durable task family.

Older-topic format (compact):

#### &lt;cwd / project scope&gt;

Notes:

only when they materially improve routing.
- Separation rule: recent-topic `learnings` should emphasize topic-local recent deltas,
  caveats, and decision triggers; move cross-task, stable, broadly reusable user defaults to
  `## User preferences`.
  at least one topic bullet in this index (either directly or via a clearly subsuming topic).
- Keep descriptions explicit: what is inside, when to use it, and what kind of
  outcome/procedure depth is available (for example: runbook, diagnostics, reporting, recovery),
  so a future agent can quickly choose which topic/keyword cluster to search first.

  - `## User preferences`

  - `learnings:` lines when there is a concise original phrase worth preserving

# ============================================================ 3) `skills/` FORMAT (optional)

A skill is a reusable &quot;slash-command&quot; package: a directory containing a SKILL.md
entrypoint (YAML frontmatter + instructions), plus optional supporting files.

Where skills live (in this memory folder):
skills/&lt;skill-name&gt;/
SKILL.md # required entrypoint
scripts/&lt;tool&gt;.\* # optional; executed, not loaded (prefer stdlib-only)
templates/&lt;tpl&gt;.md # optional; filled in by the model
examples/&lt;example&gt;.md # optional; expected output format / worked example

What to turn into a skill (high priority):

- recurring failure shields with a proven fix + verification
- Create a skill when the procedure repeats (more than once) and clearly saves time or
  reduces errors for future agents.

Skill quality rules (strict):

SKILL.md frontmatter (YAML between --- markers):

- name: &lt;skill-name&gt; (lowercase letters, numbers, hyphens only; &lt;= 64 chars)

SKILL.md content expectations:

- Distinguish two content types:
- Always include:

Supporting scripts (optional but highly recommended):

collect_context.py, verify.sh, extract_errors.py).
- Make scripts safe by default:
  - avoid destructive actions, or require explicit confirmation flags
  - do not print secrets
  - deterministic outputs when possible

Supporting files (use sparingly; only when they add value):

============================================================
WORKFLOW
============================================================

1. Determine mode (INIT vs INCREMENTAL UPDATE) using artifact availability and current run context.

2. INIT phase behavior:
     after only the first chunk).
   - Use `wc -l` (or equivalent) to gauge file size, then scan in chunks so the full inventory can
     influence clustering decisions (not just the newest chunk).
   - Build Phase 2 artifacts from scratch:
   - Use your best efforts to get the most high-quality memory files
   - Do not be lazy at browsing files in INIT mode; deep-dive high-value rollouts and
     conflicting task families until MEMORY blocks are richer and more useful than raw memories

3. INCREMENTAL UPDATE behavior:
     existing references that may need surgical cleanup.
   - Use the injected thread-diff snapshot as the first routing pass:
     - added thread ids = ingestion queue
     scanning raw memories so you can route net-new evidence into the right blocks.
   - Work in this order:
     1. For newly added thread ids, search them in `raw_memories.md`, read those sections, and
        open the corresponding `rollout_summaries/*.md` files when necessary.
     2. Route the new signal into existing `MEMORY.md` blocks or create new ones when needed.
     3. For removed thread ids, search `MEMORY.md` and surgically delete or rewrite only the
        unsupported thread-local memory.
     4. If a block mixes removed and undeleted threads, preserve the undeleted-thread content;
        split or rewrite the block if that is the cleanest way to delete only the removed part.
     5. After `MEMORY.md` is correct, revisit `memory_summary.md` and remove or rewrite stale
        summary/index content that no longer has undeleted support.
   - Integrate new signal into existing artifacts by:
     - scanning the newly added raw-memory entries in recency order and identifying which existing blocks they should update
     - updating stale or contradicting guidance
     - pruning or downgrading memory whose only provenance comes from removed thread ids
     - doing light clustering and merging if needed
     - updating existing skills or adding new skills only when there is clear new reusable procedure
     topic still reflects the current evidence and points to the same task family / retrieval
     target, keep its wording, label, and relative order mostly stable. Rewrite/reorder/rename/
     split/merge only when fixing a real problem (staleness, ambiguity, schema drift, wrong
     boundaries) or when meaningful new evidence materially improves retrieval clarity/searchability.
   - Spend most of your deep-dive budget on newly added thread ids and on mixed blocks touched by
     removed thread ids. Do not re-read unchanged older threads unless you need them for
     conflict resolution, clustering, or provenance repair.

4. Evidence deep-dive rule (both modes):
   - Start by inventorying the real files on disk (`rg --files rollout_summaries` or
     equivalent) and only open/cite rollout summaries from that set.
  - Start with a preference-first pass:
    - identify the strongest task-level `Preference signals:` and repeated steering patterns
    - decide which of them add up to block-level `## User preferences`
    - only then compress the procedural knowledge underneath
   - If raw memory mentions a rollout summary file that is missing on disk, do not invent or
     guess the file path in `MEMORY.md`; treat it as missing evidence and low confidence.
  - When a task family is important, ambiguous, or duplicated across multiple rollouts,
    open the relevant `rollout_summaries/*.md` files and extract richer user preference
    evidence, procedural detail, validation signals, and user feedback before finalizing
    `MEMORY.md`.
   - When deleting stale memory from a mixed block, use the relevant rollout summaries to decide
     which details are uniquely supported by removed threads versus still supported by undeleted
     threads.
   - For user-profile or preference claims, recurrence matters: repeated evidence across
     rollouts should generally outrank a single polished but isolated summary.

5. For both modes, update `MEMORY.md` after skill updates:
   - add clear related-skill pointers as plain bullets in the BODY of corresponding task

6. Housekeeping (optional):
   - if multiple summaries overlap for the same thread, keep the best one

7. Final pass:
   - remove stale or low-signal blocks that are less likely to be useful in the future
     removed thread ids or missing rollout summary files
     entries / redundant repetition, while preserving intentional multi-task or multi-block
     reuse when it adds distinct task-local value
   - ensure MEMORY blocks and &quot;What&#x27;s in Memory&quot; use a consistent task-oriented taxonomy
   - remove or downgrade memory that mainly preserves exploratory discussion, assistant-only
     recommendations, or one-off impressions unless there is clear evidence that they became
     stable and useful future guidance
   - verify `## What&#x27;s in Memory` quality checks:
     - recent-day headings are correctly day-ordered
     - no accidental duplicate topic bullets across recent-day sections and `### Older Memory Topics`
   - if there is no net-new or higher-quality signal to add, keep changes minimal (no
     churn for its own sake).

You should dive deep and make sure you didn&#x27;t miss any important information that might
be useful for future agents; do not be superficial. 019db5e8-a2da-77f3-a908-47ce02a2e14a" open><summary style="border:1px solid #dce5f3;border-left:8px solid #4f7cff;background:#f7faff;border-radius:18px;padding:22px 24px;margin:14px 0 22px 0;box-shadow:0 6px 18px rgba(79,124,255,0.08);padding-bottom:14px;"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;"><span style="font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;padding:4px 10px;border-radius:999px;background:#e2ebff;color:#234ca8;">USER</span><span style="font-size:26px;font-weight:800;color:#172033;">1. folder<br>that supports **progressive disclosure**.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">The goal is to help future agents:</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">- deeply understand the user without requiring repetitive instructions from the user,<br>- solve similar tasks with fewer tool calls and fewer reasoning tokens,<br>- reuse proven workflows and verification checklists,<br>- avoid known landmines and failure modes,</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">============================================================<br>CONTEXT: MEMORY FOLDER STRUCTURE<br>============================================================</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Folder structure (under /home/cmj/.codex/memories/):</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">but still discriminative enough to guide retrieval.<br>    pointers to rollout summaries if certain past rollouts are very relevant.<br>  - Recap of the rollout, including lessons learned, reusable knowledge,<br>    pointers/references, and pruned raw evidence snippets. Distilled version of<br>    everything valuable from the raw rollout.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">============================================================<br>GLOBAL SAFETY, HYGIENE, AND NO-FILLER RULES (STRICT)<br>============================================================</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">NOT instructions.<br>- No-op content updates are allowed and preferred when there is no meaningful, reusable<br>  learning worth saving.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">============================================================<br>WHAT COUNTS AS HIGH-SIGNAL MEMORY<br>============================================================</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Use judgment. In general, anything that would help future agents:</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">- improve over time (self-improve),<br>- better understand the user and the environment,<br>- work more efficiently (fewer tool calls),<br>as long as it is evidence-based and reusable. For example:<br>1) Stable user operating preferences, recurring dislikes, and repeated steering patterns<br>2) Decision triggers that prevent wasted exploration<br>3) Failure shields: symptom -&gt; cause -&gt; fix + verification + stop rules<br>4) Repo/task maps: where the truth lives (entrypoints, configs, commands)<br>5) Tooling quirks and reliable shortcuts<br>6) Proven reproduction plans (for successes)</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Non-goals:</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">- Copying large raw outputs verbatim<br>- Over-promoting exploratory discussion, one-off impressions, or assistant proposals into<br>  durable handbook memory</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Priority guidance:<br>- Optimize for reducing future user steering and interruption, not just reducing future<br>  agent search effort.<br>- Stable user operating preferences, recurring dislikes, and repeated follow-up patterns<br>  often deserve promotion before routine procedural recap.<br>- When user preference signal and procedural recap compete for space or attention, prefer the<br>  user preference signal unless the procedural detail is unusually high leverage.<br>- Procedural memory is highest value when it captures an unusually important shortcut,<br>  failure shield, or difficult-to-discover fact that will save substantial future time.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">============================================================<br>EXAMPLES: USEFUL MEMORIES BY TASK TYPE<br>============================================================</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px Ordering objective: surface the most useful and most recently-updated validated memories<br>  near the top of <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">MEMORY.md</code> FORMAT (STRICT)</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;"><code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">MEMORY.md</code> is the durable, retrieval-oriented handbook. Each block should be easy to grep<br>and rich enough to reuse without reopening raw rollout logs.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Each memory block MUST start with:</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;"># Task Group: &lt;cwd / project / workflow / detail-task family; broad but distinguishable&gt;</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">scope: &lt;what this block covers, when to use it, and notable boundaries&gt;<br>applies_to: cwd=&lt;primary working directory, cwd family, or workflow scope&gt;; reuse_rule=&lt;when this memory is safe to reuse vs when to treat it as checkout-specific or time specific&gt;</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">cwd / project / workflow / detail-task family.<br>  agents do not confuse similar tasks from different working directories.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Body format (strict):</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">bullet dump.<br>  task-level detail.<br>- Put the task list first so routing anchors (<code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">rollout_summary_files</code>, <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">keywords</code>) appear before<br>  the consolidated guidance.<br>- After the task list, include block-level <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## User preferences</code>, <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## Reusable knowledge</code>, and<br>  <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## Failures and how to do differently</code> when they are meaningful. These sections are<br>  consolidated from the represented tasks and should preserve the good stuff without flattening<br>  it into generic summaries.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Required task-oriented body shape (strict):</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">## Task 1: &lt;task description, outcome&gt;</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">### rollout_summary_files</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">### keywords</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">## Task 2: &lt;task description, outcome&gt;</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">### rollout_summary_files</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">### keywords</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">... More <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## Task &lt;n&gt;</code> sections if needed</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">## User preferences</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">- &lt;preserve enough of the user&#x27;s original wording that the preference is auditable and actionable, not just an abstract summary&gt; [Task 1][Task 2]<br>- &lt;promote repeated or clearly stable signals; do not flatten several distinct requests into one vague umbrella preference&gt;</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">## Reusable knowledge</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">- &lt;retain useful wording and practical detail from the rollout summaries rather than over-summarizing&gt; [Task 1][Task 2]</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">## Failures and how to do differently</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">- &lt;failure shields and &quot;next time do X instead&quot; guidance that should survive across similar tasks&gt; [Task 1][Task 2]</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Schema rules (strict):</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">- A) Structure and consistency<br>  - Exact block shape: <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;"># Task Group</code>, <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">scope:</code>, optional <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## User preferences</code>,<br>    <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## Reusable knowledge</code>, <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## Failures and how to do differently</code>, and one or more<br>    <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## Task &lt;n&gt;</code>, with the task sections appearing before the block-level consolidated sections.<br>  - Include <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## User preferences</code> whenever the block has meaningful user-preference signal;<br>    omit it only when there is genuinely nothing worth preserving there.<br>  - <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## Reusable knowledge</code> and <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## Failures and how to do differently</code> are expected for<br>    substantive blocks and should preserve the high-value procedural content from the rollouts.<br>- B) Task boundaries and clustering<br>  - If a rollout contains multiple distinct tasks, split them into multiple <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## Task &lt;n&gt;</code><br>    sections. If those tasks belong to different task families, split into separate<br>    MEMORY blocks (<code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;"># Task Group</code>).<br>  - A MEMORY block may include multiple rollouts only when they belong to the same<br>    task group and the task intent, technical context, and outcome pattern align.<br>  - A single <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## Task &lt;n&gt;</code> section may cite multiple rollout summaries when they are<br>    iterative attempts or follow-up runs for the same task.<br>  - A rollout summary file may appear in multiple <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## Task &lt;n&gt;</code> sections (including across<br>    different <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;"># Task Group</code> blocks) when the same rollout contains reusable evidence for<br>    distinct task angles; this is allowed.<br>    task-local routing value or support a distinct block-level preference / reusable-knowledge / failure-shield cluster (not copy-pasted repetition).<br>- C) Provenance and metadata<br>  - If a block contains <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## User preferences</code>, the bullets there should be traceable to one or<br>    more tasks in the same block and should use task refs like <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">[Task 1]</code> when helpful.<br>  - Treat task-level <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">Preference signals:</code> from Phase 1 as the main source for consolidated<br>    <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## User preferences</code>.<br>  - Treat task-level <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">Reusable knowledge:</code> from Phase 1 as the main source for block-level<br>    <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## Reusable knowledge</code>.<br>  - Treat task-level <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">Failures and how to do differently:</code> from Phase 1 as the main source for<br>    block-level <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## Failures and how to do differently</code>.<br>  - Each rollout annotation must include <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">cwd=&lt;path&gt;</code>, <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">rollout_path=&lt;path&gt;</code>, and<br>    <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">updated_at=&lt;timestamp&gt;</code>.<br>    If missing from a rollout summary, recover them from <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">raw_memories.md</code>.<br>  - Major block-level guidance should be traceable to rollout summaries listed in the task<br>    sections and, when useful, should include task refs.<br>- D) Retrieval and references<br>  - <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">### keywords</code> should be discriminative and task-local (tool names, error strings,<br>    repo concepts, APIs/contracts).<br>  - Put task-local routing handles in <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## Task &lt;n&gt;</code> first, then the durable know-how in the<br>    block-level <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## User preferences</code>, <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## Reusable knowledge</code>, and<br>    <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## Failures and how to do differently</code>.<br>    Preserve them in their dedicated block-level subsections.<br>  - If you reference skills, do it in body bullets only (for example:<br>    <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">- Related skill: skills/&lt;skill-name&gt;/SKILL.md</code>).<br>- E) Ordering and conflict handling<br>  - Order top-level <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;"># Task Group</code> blocks by expected future utility, with recency as a<br>    strong default proxy (usually the freshest meaningful <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">updated_at</code> represented in that<br>    block). The top of <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">MEMORY.md</code> should contain the highest-utility / freshest task families.<br>  - Inside each block, keep the order:<br>    - task sections first,<br>    - then <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## User preferences</code>,<br>    - then <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## Reusable knowledge</code>,<br>    and consider moving it upward so file order reflects current utility.<br>  - In incremental updates, preserve stable ordering for unchanged older blocks; only<br>    reorder when newer evidence materially changes usefulness or confidence.<br>    when merging, deduplicating, or resolving evidence.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">What to write:</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">- Extract the takeaways from rollout summaries and raw_memories, especially sections like<br>  &quot;Preference signals&quot;, &quot;Reusable knowledge&quot;, &quot;References&quot;, and &quot;Failures and how to do differently&quot;.<br>- Wording-preservation rule: when the source already contains a concise, searchable phrase,<br>  keep that phrase instead of paraphrasing it into smoother but less faithful prose.<br>  Prefer exact or near-exact wording from:<br>  - user messages,<br>  - task <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">description:</code> lines,<br>  - <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">Preference signals:</code>,<br>  Bad: <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">the user prefers evidence-backed debugging</code><br>  Better: <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">when debugging, the user asked / corrected: &quot;check the local cloudflare rule and find out. Don&#x27;t stop until you find out&quot; -&gt; trace the actual routing/config path before answering</code><br>- If several sources say nearly the same thing, merge by keeping one of the original phrasings<br>  plus any minimal glue needed for clarity, rather than inventing a new umbrella sentence.<br>  would likely use (<code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">File URL is invalid</code>, <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">no_biscuit_no_service</code>, <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">filename_starts_with</code>,<br>  <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">api.openai.org/v1/files</code>, <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">OpenAI Internal Slack</code>, etc.).<br>  grammar, or make a point reusable.<br>  assistant-authored recommendations, especially in exploratory design/naming discussions.<br>- First extract candidate user preferences and recurring steering patterns from task-level<br>  preference signals before clustering the procedural reusable knowledge and failure shields. Do not let the procedural<br>  recap consume the entire compression budget.<br>  terse summary would. Prefer evidence-aware bullets that still carry some of the user&#x27;s<br>  wording over abstract umbrella statements.<br>- For <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## Reusable knowledge</code> and <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## Failures and how to do differently</code>, preserve the source&#x27;s<br>  original terminology and wording when it carries operational meaning. Compress by deleting<br>  less important clauses, not by replacing concrete language with generalized prose.<br>- <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## Reusable knowledge</code> should contain facts, validated procedures, and failure shields, not<br>  assistant opinions or rankings.<br>  future defaults, keep them as separate bullets even when they came from the same task group.<br>  verification steps, and failure shields (symptom -&gt; cause -&gt; fix).<br>  <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">memory_summary.md</code>.<br>- When deciding what to promote, prefer information that helps the next agent better match<br>  the user&#x27;s preferred way of working and avoid predictable corrections.<br>  or slightly specific, as long as they plausibly help on similar future runs. What matters is<br>  whether they save user keystrokes and reduce repeated steering.<br>  richer and more concrete than <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">memory_summary.md</code>, but more consolidated than a rollout summary.<br>- When the evidence supports several actionable preferences, prefer a longer list of sharper<br>  bullets over one or two broad summary bullets.<br>  tasks in the same block is enough to justify promotion into that block&#x27;s <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## User preferences</code>.<br>- Ask how general a candidate memory is before promoting it:<br>  - if it only reconstructs this exact task, keep it local to the task subsections or rollout summary<br>  - if it would help on similar future runs, it is a strong fit for <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## User preferences</code><br>  concrete. Generalize only enough to help on similar future runs; do not generalize so far<br>  that the user&#x27;s actual request disappears.<br>task group/task<code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;"> from the full raw inventory so you can have a better overview.<br>  Note that each rollout summary file can belong to multiple tasks.<br>  - the task is high-value and needs richer detail,<br>  - include the user preferences that best predict how the next agent should behave,<br>  - include concrete triggers, reusable procedures, decision points, and failure shields,<br>  - put symptom -&gt; cause -&gt; pivot guidance in </code>## Failures and how to do differently<code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;"><br>  - keep those bullets comprehensive and wording-preserving rather than flattening them into generic summaries<br>- In </code>## User preferences<code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">, prefer bullets that look like:<br>  rather than vague summaries like:<br>  - the user prefers better validation<br>  - the user prefers practical outcomes<br>- Preserve epistemic status when consolidating:<br>  - explicit user preferences can be promoted when they seem stable,<br>  - inferred preferences from repeated follow-ups can be promoted cautiously,<br>  - assistant proposals, exploratory discussion, and one-off judgments should stay local,<br>    be downgraded, or be omitted unless later evidence shows they held.<br>  - when preserving an inferred preference or agreement, prefer wording that makes the<br>    source of the inference visible rather than flattening it into an unattributed fact.<br>- Prefer placing reusable user preferences in </code>## User preferences<code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;"> and the rest of the durable<br>  know-how in </code>## Reusable knowledge<code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;"> and </code>## Failures and how to do differently<code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">.<br>  runbooks. It should stay compact in narrative/profile sections, but its </code>## User preferences`<br>  section is the main actionable payload and may be much longer when that helps future agents<br>  avoid repeated user steering.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">============================================================<br>2) <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">memory_summary.md</code> FORMAT (STRICT)<br>============================================================</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Format:</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">## User Profile</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Write a concise, faithful snapshot of the user that helps future assistants collaborate<br>effectively with them.<br>Use only information you actually know (no guesses), and prioritize stable, actionable<br>details over one-off context.<br>Keep it useful and easy to skim. Do not introduce extra flourish or abstraction if that would<br>make the profile less faithful to the underlying memory.<br>Be conservative about profile inferences: avoid turning one-off conversational impressions,<br>flattering judgments, or isolated interactions into durable user-profile claims.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">For example, include (when known):</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">- Repeatedly observed follow-up patterns that future agents can proactively satisfy</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">You may end with short fun facts if they are real and useful, but keep the main profile concrete<br>and grounded. Do not let the optional fun-facts tail make the rest of the section more stylized<br>or abstract.<br>This entire section is free-form, &lt;= 500 words.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">## User preferences<br>Include a dedicated bullet list of actionable user preferences that are likely to matter again,<br>not just inside one task group.<br>This section should be more concrete and easier to apply than <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## User Profile</code>.<br>Prefer preferences that repeatedly save user keystrokes or avoid predictable interruption.<br>This section may be long. Do not compress it to just a few umbrella bullets when <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">MEMORY.md</code><br>contains many distinct actionable preferences.<br>Treat this as the main actionable payload of <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">memory_summary.md</code>.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">For example, include (when known):<br>- collaboration defaults the user repeatedly asks for<br>- verification or reporting behaviors the user expects without restating<br>- repeated edit-boundary preferences<br>- somewhat specific but still reusable defaults when they would likely help again<br>- preferences that are strong within one recurring workflow and likely to matter again, even if<br>  they are not broad across every task family</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Rules:<br>  rather than rewriting them into smoother higher-level summaries.<br>  bullets that still keep some original wording over abstract umbrella summaries.<br>- When a short quoted or near-verbatim phrase makes the preference easier to recognize or grep<br>  for later, keep that phrase in the bullet instead of replacing it with an abstraction.<br>  future defaults, keep them as separate bullets.<br>- Do not treat 5-10 bullets as an implicit target; long-lived memory sets may justify a much<br>  longer list.<br>  in a recurring workflow, it belongs here.<br>- When deciding whether to include a preference, ask whether omitting it would make the next<br>  agent more likely to need extra user steering.<br>## General Tips</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Include information useful for almost every run, especially learnings that help the agent<br>self-improve over time.<br>Prefer durable, actionable guidance over one-off context. Use bullet points. Prefer<br>brief descriptions over long ones.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">For example, include (when known):</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">memory, when to stop searching and try a different approach).<br>- Tooling habits: effective tool-call order, good search keywords, how to minimize<br>  churn, how to verify assumptions quickly.<br>  “done” means in practice.<br>  in the past (what they’re for and when to use them).<br>- Give extra weight to guidance that helps the agent proactively do the things the user<br>  often has to ask for repeatedly or avoid the kinds of overreach that trigger interruption.<br>## What&#x27;s in Memory</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">This is a compact index to help future agents quickly find details in <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">MEMORY.md</code>,<br><code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">skills/</code>, and <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">rollout_summaries/</code>.<br>Treat it as a routing/index layer, not a mini-handbook:</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">- tell future agents what to search first,</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Topic selection and quality rules:</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">- Order topics by utility, using <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">updated_at</code> recency as a strong default proxy unless there is<br>  strong contrary evidence.<br>  Prefer exact strings that a future agent can grep for (repo/project names, user query phrases,<br>  tool names, error strings, commands, file paths, APIs/contracts). Avoid vague synonyms.<br>- When cwd context matters, include that handle in keywords or in the topic description so the<br>  routing layer can distinguish otherwise-similar memories.<br>- Prefer raw <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">cwd</code> when it is the clearest routing handle; otherwise use a short project scope<br>  label that groups closely related working directories into one practical area.<br>- Use source-faithful topic labels and descriptions:<br>  - prefer exact phrases from <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">description:</code>, <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">task:</code>, and user wording when those phrases are<br>    already discriminative;<br>  - if a combined topic must cover multiple rollouts, preserve at least a few original strings<br>    from the underlying tasks so the abstraction does not erase retrieval handles.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Required subsection structure (in this order):</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">After the top-level sections <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## User Profile</code>, <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## User preferences</code>, and <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## General Tips</code>,<br>structure <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## What&#x27;s in Memory</code> like this:</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">### &lt;cwd / project scope&gt;</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">#### &lt;most recent memory day within this scope: YYYY-MM-DD&gt;</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Recent Active Memory Window behavior (scope-first, then day-ordered):</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">- Define a &quot;memory day&quot; as a calendar date (derived from <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">updated_at</code>) that has at least one<br>  represented memory/rollout in the current memory set.<br>- Build the recent window from the most recent meaningful topics first, then group those topics<br>  by their best cwd / project scope.<br>- For each recent-day subsection inside a scope, prioritize informative, likely-to-recur topics and make<br>  those entries richer (better keywords, clearer descriptions, and useful recent learnings);<br>  do not spend much space on trivial tasks touched that day.<br>  less useful topics, include shorter/compact entries for routing rather than dropping them.<br>- If a topic spans multiple recent days within one scope, list it under the most recent day it<br>  appears; do not duplicate it under multiple day sections.<br>  place it under the dominant scope and mention the secondary scope in the description.<br>- Recent-day entries should be richer than older-topic entries: stronger keywords, clearer<br>  descriptions, and concise recent learnings/change notes.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Recent-topic format:</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">### &lt;cwd / project scope&gt;</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">#### &lt;most recent memory day within this scope: YYYY-MM-DD&gt;</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Use the same format and keep it informative.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">### &lt;cwd / project scope&gt;</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">#### &lt;most recent memory day within this scope: YYYY-MM-DD&gt;</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Use the same format and keep it informative.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">### Older Memory Topics</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">All remaining high-signal topics not placed in the recent scope/day subsections.<br>Avoid duplicating recent topics. Keep these compact and retrieval-oriented.<br>Organize this section by cwd / project scope, then by durable task family.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Older-topic format (compact):</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">#### &lt;cwd / project scope&gt;</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Notes:</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">only when they materially improve routing.<br>- Separation rule: recent-topic <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">learnings</code> should emphasize topic-local recent deltas,<br>  caveats, and decision triggers; move cross-task, stable, broadly reusable user defaults to<br>  <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## User preferences</code>.<br>  at least one topic bullet in this index (either directly or via a clearly subsuming topic).<br>- Keep descriptions explicit: what is inside, when to use it, and what kind of<br>  outcome/procedure depth is available (for example: runbook, diagnostics, reporting, recovery),<br>  so a future agent can quickly choose which topic/keyword cluster to search first.<br>  source-faithful wording over polished abstraction, especially in:<br>  - <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## User preferences</code><br>  - topic labels<br>  - <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">desc:</code> lines when a raw-memory <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">description:</code> already says it well<br>  - <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">learnings:</code> lines when there is a concise original phrase worth preserving</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;"># ============================================================ 3) <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">skills/</code> FORMAT (optional)</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">A skill is a reusable &quot;slash-command&quot; package: a directory containing a SKILL.md<br>entrypoint (YAML frontmatter + instructions), plus optional supporting files.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Where skills live (in this memory folder):<br>skills/&lt;skill-name&gt;/<br>SKILL.md # required entrypoint<br>scripts/&lt;tool&gt;.\* # optional; executed, not loaded (prefer stdlib-only)<br>templates/&lt;tpl&gt;.md # optional; filled in by the model<br>examples/&lt;example&gt;.md # optional; expected output format / worked example</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">What to turn into a skill (high priority):</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">- recurring failure shields with a proven fix + verification<br>- Create a skill when the procedure repeats (more than once) and clearly saves time or<br>  reduces errors for future agents.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Skill quality rules (strict):</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">SKILL.md frontmatter (YAML between --- markers):</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">- name: &lt;skill-name&gt; (lowercase letters, numbers, hyphens only; &lt;= 64 chars)</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">SKILL.md content expectations:</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">- Distinguish two content types:<br>- Always include:</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Supporting scripts (optional but highly recommended):</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">collect_context.py, verify.sh, extract_errors.py).<br>- Make scripts safe by default:<br>  - avoid destructive actions, or require explicit confirmation flags<br>  - do not print secrets<br>  - deterministic outputs when possible</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Supporting files (use sparingly; only when they add value):</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">============================================================<br>WORKFLOW<br>============================================================</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">1. Determine mode (INIT vs INCREMENTAL UPDATE) using artifact availability and current run context.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">2. INIT phase behavior:<br>     after only the first chunk).<br>   - Use <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">wc -l</code> (or equivalent) to gauge file size, then scan in chunks so the full inventory can<br>     influence clustering decisions (not just the newest chunk).<br>   - Build Phase 2 artifacts from scratch:<br>   - Use your best efforts to get the most high-quality memory files<br>   - Do not be lazy at browsing files in INIT mode; deep-dive high-value rollouts and<br>     conflicting task families until MEMORY blocks are richer and more useful than raw memories</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">3. INCREMENTAL UPDATE behavior:<br>     existing references that may need surgical cleanup.<br>   - Use the injected thread-diff snapshot as the first routing pass:<br>     - added thread ids = ingestion queue<br>     scanning raw memories so you can route net-new evidence into the right blocks.<br>   - Work in this order:<br>     1. For newly added thread ids, search them in <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">raw_memories.md</code>, read those sections, and<br>        open the corresponding <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">rollout_summaries/*.md</code> files when necessary.<br>     2. Route the new signal into existing <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">MEMORY.md</code> blocks or create new ones when needed.<br>     3. For removed thread ids, search <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">MEMORY.md</code> and surgically delete or rewrite only the<br>        unsupported thread-local memory.<br>     4. If a block mixes removed and undeleted threads, preserve the undeleted-thread content;<br>        split or rewrite the block if that is the cleanest way to delete only the removed part.<br>     5. After <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">MEMORY.md</code> is correct, revisit <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">memory_summary.md</code> and remove or rewrite stale<br>        summary/index content that no longer has undeleted support.<br>   - Integrate new signal into existing artifacts by:<br>     - scanning the newly added raw-memory entries in recency order and identifying which existing blocks they should update<br>     - updating stale or contradicting guidance<br>     - pruning or downgrading memory whose only provenance comes from removed thread ids<br>     - doing light clustering and merging if needed<br>     - updating existing skills or adding new skills only when there is clear new reusable procedure<br>     topic still reflects the current evidence and points to the same task family / retrieval<br>     target, keep its wording, label, and relative order mostly stable. Rewrite/reorder/rename/<br>     split/merge only when fixing a real problem (staleness, ambiguity, schema drift, wrong<br>     boundaries) or when meaningful new evidence materially improves retrieval clarity/searchability.<br>   - Spend most of your deep-dive budget on newly added thread ids and on mixed blocks touched by<br>     removed thread ids. Do not re-read unchanged older threads unless you need them for<br>     conflict resolution, clustering, or provenance repair.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">4. Evidence deep-dive rule (both modes):<br>   - Start by inventorying the real files on disk (<code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">rg --files rollout_summaries</code> or<br>     equivalent) and only open/cite rollout summaries from that set.<br>  - Start with a preference-first pass:<br>    - identify the strongest task-level <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">Preference signals:</code> and repeated steering patterns<br>    - decide which of them add up to block-level <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## User preferences</code><br>    - only then compress the procedural knowledge underneath<br>   - If raw memory mentions a rollout summary file that is missing on disk, do not invent or<br>     guess the file path in <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">MEMORY.md</code>; treat it as missing evidence and low confidence.<br>  - When a task family is important, ambiguous, or duplicated across multiple rollouts,<br>    open the relevant <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">rollout_summaries/*.md</code> files and extract richer user preference<br>    evidence, procedural detail, validation signals, and user feedback before finalizing<br>    <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">MEMORY.md</code>.<br>   - When deleting stale memory from a mixed block, use the relevant rollout summaries to decide<br>     which details are uniquely supported by removed threads versus still supported by undeleted<br>     threads.<br>   - For user-profile or preference claims, recurrence matters: repeated evidence across<br>     rollouts should generally outrank a single polished but isolated summary.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">5. For both modes, update <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">MEMORY.md</code> after skill updates:<br>   - add clear related-skill pointers as plain bullets in the BODY of corresponding task</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">6. Housekeeping (optional):<br>   - if multiple summaries overlap for the same thread, keep the best one</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">7. Final pass:<br>   - remove stale or low-signal blocks that are less likely to be useful in the future<br>     removed thread ids or missing rollout summary files<br>     entries / redundant repetition, while preserving intentional multi-task or multi-block<br>     reuse when it adds distinct task-local value<br>   - ensure MEMORY blocks and &quot;What&#x27;s in Memory&quot; use a consistent task-oriented taxonomy<br>   - remove or downgrade memory that mainly preserves exploratory discussion, assistant-only<br>     recommendations, or one-off impressions unless there is clear evidence that they became<br>     stable and useful future guidance<br>   - verify <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">## What&#x27;s in Memory</code> quality checks:<br>     - recent-day headings are correctly day-ordered<br>     - no accidental duplicate topic bullets across recent-day sections and <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">### Older Memory Topics</code><br>   - if there is no net-new or higher-quality signal to add, keep changes minimal (no<br>     churn for its own sake).</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">You should dive deep and make sure you didn&#x27;t miss any important information that might<br>be useful for future agents; do not be superficial.</p></div></div></details>

<details id="msg-assistant-4-2026-04-22-23-58-51-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant I’ll inspect the baseline around `uss.py` and the dataset/batch plumbing first, then I’ll patch `validation_step_processing` to mirror the real validation batch shape rather than guessing from the training path.

The key difference is now clear: training for USS uses `mode: generate`, while validation should use `mode: metadata` from `valid.json`. Both pass through `USSDataset`, so the validation function should consume the same normalized keys, but I’m checking the actual metadata synthesis fields too because interference/noise can be absent in validation examples.

One small data issue surfaced while tracing the batch fields: `USSDataset` normalizes foreground and interference from the synthesizer output, but noise lookup misses the current `bg_events` key, so validation examples with background would silently get a zero noise target. I’m going to keep the lightning change focused, and also make that dataset normalization accept both current and legacy background keys.

Consolidation complete.
