Implemented it.

In [uss.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/training/lightningmodule/uss.py:5), I added a shared `_get_target_dict()` and a `validation_step_processing()` that mirrors training, converts losses to Python floats for Lightning logging, and appends optional metrics just like the other baseline lightning modules.

I also fixed one related data-normalization issue in [uss_dataset.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/datamodules/uss_dataset.py:39): validation/training synthesis outputs use `bg_events`, but USS dataset only checked older `background` / `bg_event` keys, so noise targets could silently become zero.

<details id="msg-assistant-14-2026-04-23-22-54-07-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant I’ll trace `self.K` through `resunet_mod.py` to see whether it’s a fixed architectural constant, a channel/group multiplier, or tied to the ResUNet block design.

`self.K = 3` is the number of mask feature maps predicted per target source per input channel.

In [resunet_mod.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/resunet2/resunet_mod.py:280), it is used here:

`input_channels * K * target_sources_num` channels.
  `[B, target_sources_num, input_channels, K, T, F]`.
- Then the three `K` slices are interpreted as:

So the model predicts:

```text
K = 3 = [mask_mag, mask_real, mask_imag]
```

The real/imag mask pair is normalized with `magphase()` to produce `mask_cos` and `mask_sin`, then it rotates the input mixture phase:

```python
out_cos = cos_in * mask_cos - sin_in * mask_sin
out_sin = sin_in * mask_cos + cos_in * mask_sin
```

Then `out_mag = input_mag * mask_mag`, and ISTFT reconstructs waveform.

There is also a clue in the code:

```python
# linear_mag = torch.tanh(x[:, :, :, 3, :, :])
# out_mag = F.relu_(sp[:, None, :, :, :] * mask_mag + linear_mag)
```

That commented path would require `K = 4`, adding an extra linear magnitude residual. <meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-16-2026-04-23-23-01-38-cst-" data-role="assistant" data-label="16. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-16-2026-04-23-23-01-38-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant I’ll compare the two decoder heads directly: what each predicts from latent features, how masks are constrained, how phase is handled, and what waveform reconstruction path they use. Then I’ll give a concrete recommendation for whether `ModifiedDeFTUSS` should borrow anything from ResUNet’s final stage.

Yes. `ModifiedDeFTUSS` probably deserves a small final-stage improvement.

**Key Difference**
`ResUNet30_Base` predicts **3 mask components** per source/channel:

```text
[mask_mag, mask_real, mask_imag]
```

Then it uses:
- `sigmoid(mask_mag)` for nonnegative magnitude masking
- normalized `(mask_real, mask_imag)` as a phase-rotation mask
- `out_conv` to combine multi-channel estimates into output channels

See [resunet_mod.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/resunet2/resunet_mod.py:478).

`ModifiedDeFTUSS` predicts only **2 mask components**:

```text
[complex_mask_real, complex_mask_imag]
```

Then directly applies them as a complex mask to only the reference channel:

```python
est_real = mask_r * ref_real - mask_i * ref_imag
est_imag = mask_r * ref_imag + mask_i * ref_real
```

See [modified_deft.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/deft/modified_deft.py:175).

**Which Is Better?**
For final audio reconstruction, `ResUNet30_Base` is better designed.

Reasons:

`ModifiedDeFTUSS` is simpler but weaker:

**Recommendation**
I would improve `ModifiedDeFTUSS` by changing its final `audio_head` from 2 outputs to 3 outputs:

```text
[mask_mag, mask_real, mask_imag]
```

Then reconstruct like ResUNet:

```python
mask_mag = torch.sigmoid(mask[:, :, 0])
mask_real = torch.tanh(mask[:, :, 1])
mask_imag = torch.tanh(mask[:, :, 2])
_, mask_cos, mask_sin = magphase(mask_real, mask_imag)

out_mag = ref_mag * mask_mag
out_phase = ref_phase + mask_phase
```

A bigger improvement would also add a small `out_conv` so `ModifiedDeFTUSS` can reconstruct from all mixture channels, not just channel 0. But the safer first step is the `K=3` magnitude-plus-phase head. It should be compatible with the current waveform losses and output dict. 019db5e7-f91d-7200-8dc8-9f047e8df20c" open><summary style="border:1px solid #d7eadf;border-left:8px solid #3fa56b;background:#f5fcf7;border-radius:18px;padding:22px 24px;margin:14px 0 22px 0;box-shadow:0 6px 18px rgba(63,165,107,0.08);padding-bottom:14px;"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;"><span style="font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;padding:4px 10px;border-radius:999px;background:#dff5e7;color:#1c6b41;">ASSISTANT</span><span style="font-size:26px;font-weight:800;color:#172033;">16. components**:</p><div class="code-block" style="margin:10px 0 18px 0;border:1px solid #d6dce8;border-radius:14px;overflow:hidden;box-shadow:inset 0 1px 0 rgba(255,255,255,0.5);"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;background:#1f2937;color:#e5edf7;font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;text-transform:uppercase;padding:9px 12px;"><span>text</span><button class="copy-btn" type="button" onclick="copyCode(this)">Copy</button></div><pre style="margin:0;background:#0f1720;color:#e8eef6;padding:16px 18px;overflow:auto;font-size:14px;line-height:1.6;"><code>[complex_mask_real, complex_mask_imag]</code></pre></div><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Then directly applies them as a complex mask to only the reference channel:</p><div class="code-block" style="margin:10px 0 18px 0;border:1px solid #d6dce8;border-radius:14px;overflow:hidden;box-shadow:inset 0 1px 0 rgba(255,255,255,0.5);"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;background:#1f2937;color:#e5edf7;font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;text-transform:uppercase;padding:9px 12px;"><span>python</span><button class="copy-btn" type="button" onclick="copyCode(this)">Copy</button></div><pre style="margin:0;background:#0f1720;color:#e8eef6;padding:16px 18px;overflow:auto;font-size:14px;line-height:1.6;"><code>est_real = mask_r * ref_real - mask_i * ref_imag
est_imag = mask_r * ref_imag + mask_i * ref_real</code></pre></div><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">See [modified_deft.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/deft/modified_deft.py:175).</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">**Which Is Better?**<br>For final audio reconstruction, <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">ResUNet30_Base</code> is better designed.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Reasons:</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;"><code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">ModifiedDeFTUSS</code> is simpler but weaker:</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">**Recommendation**<br>I would improve <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">ModifiedDeFTUSS</code> by changing its final <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">audio_head</code> from 2 outputs to 3 outputs:</p><div class="code-block" style="margin:10px 0 18px 0;border:1px solid #d6dce8;border-radius:14px;overflow:hidden;box-shadow:inset 0 1px 0 rgba(255,255,255,0.5);"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;background:#1f2937;color:#e5edf7;font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;text-transform:uppercase;padding:9px 12px;"><span>text</span><button class="copy-btn" type="button" onclick="copyCode(this)">Copy</button></div><pre style="margin:0;background:#0f1720;color:#e8eef6;padding:16px 18px;overflow:auto;font-size:14px;line-height:1.6;"><code>[mask_mag, mask_real, mask_imag]</code></pre></div><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Then reconstruct like ResUNet:</p><div class="code-block" style="margin:10px 0 18px 0;border:1px solid #d6dce8;border-radius:14px;overflow:hidden;box-shadow:inset 0 1px 0 rgba(255,255,255,0.5);"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;background:#1f2937;color:#e5edf7;font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;text-transform:uppercase;padding:9px 12px;"><span>python</span><button class="copy-btn" type="button" onclick="copyCode(this)">Copy</button></div><pre style="margin:0;background:#0f1720;color:#e8eef6;padding:16px 18px;overflow:auto;font-size:14px;line-height:1.6;"><code>mask_mag = torch.sigmoid(mask[:, :, 0])
mask_real = torch.tanh(mask[:, :, 1])
mask_imag = torch.tanh(mask[:, :, 2])
_, mask_cos, mask_sin = magphase(mask_real, mask_imag)

out_mag = ref_mag * mask_mag
out_phase = ref_phase + mask_phase</code></pre></div><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">A bigger improvement would also add a small <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">out_conv</code> so <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">ModifiedDeFTUSS</code> can reconstruct from all mixture channels, not just channel 0. But the safer first step is the <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">K=3</code> magnitude-plus-phase head. It should be compatible with the current waveform losses and output dict.</p></div></div></details>

<details id="msg-assistant-20-2026-04-23-23-15-26-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant I’ll run a CPU-only mini sanity check with the new spatial USS class: fixed synthetic batches, batch size 1, a few optimizer steps, and paired train-mode vs eval-mode loss measurements on the same tensors. That should tell us whether the training and validation loss code paths are consistent, while also separating expected BatchNorm mode differences from actual loss bugs.

The first run shows the code is stable and finite, but train-mode and eval-mode losses are not identical because this model has BatchNorm and the synthetic random noise term is especially sensitive. I’ll do one more isolation check: call the training and validation processing functions in the same model mode on the same batch, which verifies whether the two loss code paths themselves match.

Tested with CPU-only tiny `ModifiedDeFTUSSSpatial`, batch size 1, synthetic data.

The important result: **the training and validation loss code paths match exactly when evaluated in the same model mode on the same batch**:

```text
loss diff        0.00000000
loss_ce diff     0.00000000
loss_fg diff     0.00000000
loss_int diff    0.00000000
loss_noise diff  0.00000000
loss_silence diff 0.00000000
```

So `USSLightning.training_step_processing()` and `validation_step_processing()` are consistent.

I also ran 3 tiny optimizer steps in train mode and compared train-mode vs eval-mode losses on the same probe batch. They were close but not identical:

```text
initial total loss: train=3.716110 eval=4.100466 diff=0.384356
post-step total loss: train=3.691308 eval=3.940631 diff=0.249322
```

This difference is expected because the model contains `BatchNorm2d`: training uses batch statistics, evaluation uses running statistics. With batch size 1 and random synthetic waveforms, that gap can be noticeable. The `loss_noise` component differed more, but it is weighted by `lambda_non_foreground=0.01`, so its effect on total loss is small.

Conclusion: the loss implementation is behaving correctly. The direct model and lightning/loss smoke tests passed. One config-instantiation helper used the wrong key for the evaluation YAML, so I’m correcting that check now; the training YAML already instantiates as `DeFTTSELikeSpatial`.

Yes, `deft_tse.py` was too simple in the same final-stage sense.

The original `DeFTTSELike` did use spatial clues in the latent features:
- 4-channel log magnitudes

But final reconstruction still used only the reference channel:

```python
ref_real = real[:, 0]
ref_imag = imag[:, 0]
```

So spatial information could influence the mask, but the actual complex synthesis was still channel-0-only. For Task 4 same-class separation, that is weaker than it should be.

I added a stronger version:

- Predicts `3` mask components per target and input channel:
  `[magnitude_mask, phase_mask_real, phase_mask_imag]`
- Applies phase-aware reconstruction over all mixture channels
- Adds learned complex projection `out_conv: 4 -&gt; 1` before ISTFT

I also wired it into:

Validation passed:
- Tiny CPU forward:
  - `waveform (2, 3, 1, 256)`
  - finite output
  - `mask_head_out = 12` for `4 channels * 3 mask components`
  - `out_conv = 4 -&gt; 1`
  - scalar `loss`
  - float and finite

For Task 4 same-class separation, that is weaker than it should be.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">I added a stronger version:</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">- Predicts <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">3</code> mask components per target and input channel:<br>  <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">[magnitude_mask, phase_mask_real, phase_mask_imag]</code><br>- Applies phase-aware reconstruction over all mixture channels<br>- Adds learned complex projection <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">out_conv: 4 -&gt; 1</code> before ISTFT</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">I also wired it into:</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Validation passed:<br>- Tiny CPU forward:<br>  - <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">waveform (2, 3, 1, 256)</code><br>  - finite output<br>  - <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">mask_head_out = 12</code> for <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">4 channels * 3 mask components</code><br>  - <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">out_conv = 4 -&gt; 1</code><br>  - scalar <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">loss</code><br>  - float and finite</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">So now both the USS-like and TSE-like DeFT models have the stronger spatial final stage.</p></div></div></details>

<meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-26-2026-04-23-23-40-09-cst-" data-role="assistant" data-label="26. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-26-2026-04-23-23-40-09-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant I’ll trace the tensor shapes for a real 10s/32k setup and estimate activation/attention memory block by block. The parameter count can be tiny while attention activations are enormous, so I’ll focus on runtime tensors rather than weights.

I checked `ModifiedDeFTUSS`, and the 96 GB GPU memory is very plausible. The model has few parameters, but its **activation memory explodes** because each `DeFTBlock` runs full Transformer attention over the raw STFT time and frequency axes.

The key issue is in [modified_deft.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/deft/modified_deft.py:37):

```python
x_f = x.permute(0, 2, 3, 1).reshape(batch_size * time_steps, freq_bins, channels)
x_f = self.freq_attn(x_f)

x_t = x.permute(0, 3, 2, 1).reshape(batch_size * freq_bins, time_steps, channels)
x_t = self.time_attn(x_t)
```

For your setting:

```text
10s audio, sr=32000, n_fft=1024, hop=320
T ~= 1001 frames
F = 513 bins
batch = 2
heads = 4
blocks = 6
```

Estimated attention-memory pressure:

```text
freq attention per block: ~7.85 GiB fp32 attention weights
time attention per block: ~15.32 GiB fp32 attention weights
6 blocks attention weights only: ~139 GiB fp32
6 blocks attention weights only: ~69.5 GiB fp16
```

That estimate excludes Q/K/V tensors, MLP activations, conv activations, STFT tensors, gradients, optimizer state, logits, and loss-side tensors. So seeing ~96 GB during training is not surprising.

The important point: **parameter count is misleading here**. Memory is dominated by `O(B * heads * T * F * (T + F))` attention activations, not by weights.

The new `ModifiedDeFTUSSSpatial` head I added earlier is **not the main cause**. It adds larger final masks and all-channel reconstruction, but the memory explosion already exists before that, inside the axial Transformer blocks.

Best fixes, in priority order:

1. Use shorter training chunks.
   For example, 10s to 5s cuts time-attention memory about 4x; 10s to 2.5s cuts it about 16x.

2. Increase `hop_size`.
   `hop=640` roughly halves `T`, which cuts time attention about 4x. `hop=1280` cuts it about 16x. Quality tradeoff exists.

3. Do not train this model with `precision: 32-true`.
   The current config uses fp32; use `16-mixed` or `bf16-mixed` on GPU.

4. Reduce `n_deft_blocks`.
   Going from 6 to 2 blocks gives about 3x lower block activation memory.

5. The real architectural fix is to replace full global time/frequency attention with a memory-safe DeFT block:
   local/windowed time attention, downsampled attention, or chunked attention. That would preserve the spatial masking improvement while making 10s training realistic.

My recommendation: keep the spatial 3-output mask design, but make a new `ModifiedDeFTUSSSpatialLite` / `ModifiedDeFTUSSMemoryEfficient` variant where the DeFT block uses windowed time attention and optionally frequency grouping. That is the correct fix for Task4-scale 10s mixtures. 019db5e7-f91d-7200-8dc8-9f047e8df20c" open><summary style="border:1px solid #d7eadf;border-left:8px solid #3fa56b;background:#f5fcf7;border-radius:18px;padding:22px 24px;margin:14px 0 22px 0;box-shadow:0 6px 18px rgba(63,165,107,0.08);padding-bottom:14px;"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;"><span style="font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;padding:4px 10px;border-radius:999px;background:#dff5e7;color:#1c6b41;">ASSISTANT</span><span style="font-size:26px;font-weight:800;color:#172033;">26. Assistant</span><span class="summary-chevron">&#8250;</span></div></summary><div style="border:1px solid #d7eadf;border-left:8px solid #3fa56b;background:#f5fcf7;border-radius:18px;padding:22px 24px;margin:14px 0 22px 0;box-shadow:0 6px 18px rgba(63,165,107,0.08);margin-top:-8px;"><div style="display:flex;flex-wrap:wrap;gap:10px;"><div style="min-width:180px;flex:1 1 220px;background:rgba(255,255,255,0.72);border-radius:12px;padding:10px 12px;"><div style="font-size:11px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;color:#5a6b85;text-transform:uppercase;">Time</div><div style="font-size:15px;font-weight:600;color:#223049;margin-top:4px;">2026-04-23 23:40:09 CST -&gt; 2026-04-23 23:41:25 CST</div></div><div style="min-width:180px;flex:1 1 220px;background:rgba(255,255,255,0.72);border-radius:12px;padding:10px 12px;"><div style="font-size:11px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;color:#5a6b85;text-transform:uppercase;">Source</div><div style="font-size:15px;font-weight:600;color:#223049;margin-top:4px;">rollout-2026-04-22T23-56-11-019db5e7-f91d-7200-8dc8-9f047e8df20c.jsonl</div></div><div style="min-width:180px;flex:1 1 220px;background:rgba(255,255,255,0.72);border-radius:12px;padding:10px 12px;"><div style="font-size:11px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;color:#5a6b85;text-transform:uppercase;">Session</div><div style="font-size:15px;font-weight:600;color:#223049;margin-top:4px;">019db5e7-f91d-7200-8dc8-9f047e8df20c</div></div></div><div class="message-body" style="margin-top:16px;font-size:17px;line-height:1.75;color:#1d2738;white-space:pre-wrap;"><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">I’ll trace the tensor shapes for a real 10s/32k setup and estimate activation/attention memory block by block. The parameter count can be tiny while attention activations are enormous, so I’ll focus on runtime tensors rather than weights.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">I checked <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">ModifiedDeFTUSS</code>, and the 96 GB GPU memory is very plausible. The model has few parameters, but its **activation memory explodes** because each <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">DeFTBlock</code> runs full Transformer attention over the raw STFT time and frequency axes.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">The key issue is in [modified_deft.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/deft/modified_deft.py:37):</p><div class="code-block" style="margin:10px 0 18px 0;border:1px solid #d6dce8;border-radius:14px;overflow:hidden;box-shadow:inset 0 1px 0 rgba(255,255,255,0.5);"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;background:#1f2937;color:#e5edf7;font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;text-transform:uppercase;padding:9px 12px;"><span>python</span><button class="copy-btn" type="button" onclick="copyCode(this)">Copy</button></div><pre style="margin:0;background:#0f1720;color:#e8eef6;padding:16px 18px;overflow:auto;font-size:14px;line-height:1.6;"><code>x_f = x.permute(0, 2, 3, 1).reshape(batch_size * time_steps, freq_bins, channels)
x_f = self.freq_attn(x_f)

x_t = x.permute(0, 3, 2, 1).reshape(batch_size * freq_bins, time_steps, channels)
x_t = self.time_attn(x_t)</code></pre></div><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">For your setting:</p><div class="code-block" style="margin:10px 0 18px 0;border:1px solid #d6dce8;border-radius:14px;overflow:hidden;box-shadow:inset 0 1px 0 rgba(255,255,255,0.5);"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;background:#1f2937;color:#e5edf7;font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;text-transform:uppercase;padding:9px 12px;"><span>text</span><button class="copy-btn" type="button" onclick="copyCode(this)">Copy</button></div><pre style="margin:0;background:#0f1720;color:#e8eef6;padding:16px 18px;overflow:auto;font-size:14px;line-height:1.6;"><code>10s audio, sr=32000, n_fft=1024, hop=320
T ~= 1001 frames
F = 513 bins
batch = 2
heads = 4
blocks = 6</code></pre></div><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Estimated attention-memory pressure:</p><div class="code-block" style="margin:10px 0 18px 0;border:1px solid #d6dce8;border-radius:14px;overflow:hidden;box-shadow:inset 0 1px 0 rgba(255,255,255,0.5);"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;background:#1f2937;color:#e5edf7;font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;text-transform:uppercase;padding:9px 12px;"><span>text</span><button class="copy-btn" type="button" onclick="copyCode(this)">Copy</button></div><pre style="margin:0;background:#0f1720;color:#e8eef6;padding:16px 18px;overflow:auto;font-size:14px;line-height:1.6;"><code>freq attention per block: ~7.85 GiB fp32 attention weights
time attention per block: ~15.32 GiB fp32 attention weights
6 blocks attention weights only: ~139 GiB fp32
6 blocks attention weights only: ~69.5 GiB fp16</code></pre></div><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">That estimate excludes Q/K/V tensors, MLP activations, conv activations, STFT tensors, gradients, optimizer state, logits, and loss-side tensors. So seeing ~96 GB during training is not surprising.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">The important point: **parameter count is misleading here**. Memory is dominated by <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">O(B * heads * T * F * (T + F))</code> attention activations, not by weights.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">The new <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">ModifiedDeFTUSSSpatial</code> head I added earlier is **not the main cause**. It adds larger final masks and all-channel reconstruction, but the memory explosion already exists before that, inside the axial Transformer blocks.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Best fixes, in priority order:</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">1. Use shorter training chunks.<br>   For example, 10s to 5s cuts time-attention memory about 4x; 10s to 2.5s cuts it about 16x.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">2. Increase <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">hop_size</code>.<br>   <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">hop=640</code> roughly halves <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">T</code>, which cuts time attention about 4x. <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">hop=1280</code> cuts it about 16x. Quality tradeoff exists.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">3. Do not train this model with <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">precision: 32-true</code>.<br>   The current config uses fp32; use <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">16-mixed</code> or <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">bf16-mixed</code> on GPU.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">4. Reduce <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">n_deft_blocks</code>.<br>   Going from 6 to 2 blocks gives about 3x lower block activation memory.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">5. The real architectural fix is to replace full global time/frequency attention with a memory-safe DeFT block:<br>   local/windowed time attention, downsampled attention, or chunked attention. That would preserve the spatial masking improvement while making 10s training realistic.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">My recommendation: keep the spatial 3-output mask design, but make a new <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">ModifiedDeFTUSSSpatialLite</code> / <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">ModifiedDeFTUSSMemoryEfficient</code> variant where the DeFT block uses windowed time attention and optionally frequency grouping. That is the correct fix for Task4-scale 10s mixtures.</p></div></div></details>

<meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-30-2026-04-24-00-00-47-cst" data-role="assistant" data-label="30. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-30-2026-04-24-00-00-47-cst" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant Yes, it can affect SA-SDR, but the impact depends on how the model uses temporal context.

For this `ModifiedDeFTUSS` family, the risk is real because the DeFT blocks use attention over the STFT time axis. Training on 5s teaches the model to separate sources with about 5s of temporal context, while full 10s inference exposes longer structures and potentially different event layouts. With the chunked 10s inference I added, each USS chunk is still close to the training condition: `6s` chunk with `5s` hop. That should be more stable than feeding a full 10s spectrogram to a model trained only on 5s.

Expected effects:

For SA-SDR specifically, I would expect 5s training + 6s chunked inference to be much better than forcing full 10s training if the latter causes tiny batch size, OOM, or unstable optimization. But it may underperform a true 10s-trained model if memory were unlimited.

A good compromise is probably:

```yaml
training duration: 6.0
max_event_dur: 6.0
inference_chunk_seconds: 6.0 or 7.0
inference_chunk_hop_seconds: 5.0
```

6s training matches the inference chunk better and still cuts attention memory a lot compared with 10s. For final evaluation, compare:

1. train 5s, infer 6s chunks
2. train 6s, infer 6s/7s chunks
3. train 5s, infer full 10s if GPU allows eval

My guess: **6s training + chunked 10s inference** will be the safest balance for SA-SDR. 019db5e7-f91d-7200-8dc8-9f047e8df20c" open><summary style="border:1px solid #d7eadf;border-left:8px solid #3fa56b;background:#f5fcf7;border-radius:18px;padding:22px 24px;margin:14px 0 22px 0;box-shadow:0 6px 18px rgba(63,165,107,0.08);padding-bottom:14px;"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;"><span style="font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;padding:4px 10px;border-radius:999px;background:#dff5e7;color:#1c6b41;">ASSISTANT</span><span style="font-size:26px;font-weight:800;color:#172033;">30. The second stub found a small robustness issue in the new multi-crop helper: it assumes `cfg.sample_rate` is present, which is true after the real M2D mel frontend is built, but brittle for tests or unusual initialization. I’m making that fallback explicit.

One important finding popped out while testing the “strong” path: the existing `finetuning_layers=&quot;2_blocks&quot;` logic in `M2DSingleClassifier` was not actually unfreezing the last two M2D transformer blocks; it was mostly training the output norms/head. That is a real strength limiter, so I’m fixing the layer-selection logic in both the old and strong classifier classes.

The rerun passed, and the dummy check confirms `finetuning_layers: 2_blocks` now makes blocks 10 and 11 trainable. I’m adding that note to the recipe guide because it changes how to interpret older classifier runs.

Yes, the original [m2d_sc.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/m2dat/m2d_sc.py:49) was too simple for a top-rank attempt. It mean-pooled M2D tokens into one vector, used a shallow projection + ArcFace, and its `2_blocks` fine-tuning setting was not actually unfreezing the last two transformer blocks. That last one is a real bug/limiter.

I added a stronger classifier path:

- attentive statistics pooling over M2D time tokens
  - MLP projection before ArcFace
  - dropout + weight decay configs
  - optional multi-crop prediction for long source estimates

Added configs:

<meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-44-2026-04-24-00-35-13-cst-" data-role="assistant" data-label="44. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-44-2026-04-24-00-35-13-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant Yes, it’s possible, and it’s probably one of the most worthwhile classifier-side upgrades. I’m just letting the cache-export smoke test finish, then I’ll answer with the practical model choices and how I’d integrate one without breaking the current M2D-SC path.

Yes. It is possible, and for top-rank classification I think it is worth doing.

Officially, DCASE 2026 Task 4 allows pretrained models if they are on the allowed external-resource list or added before the lock date. The current Task 4 page already lists **AST**, **BEATs**, **Audio Teacher-Student Transformer**, and **Effective Pre-Training of Audio Transformers for SED** among allowed model resources. It also says embeddings from externally pretrained models count as external data and must be listed in the submission YAML. Sources: DCASE Task 4 external resources/rules: https://dcase.community/challenge2026/task-spatial-semantic-segmentation-of-sound-scenes

My recommendation:

1. **Best first upgrade: BEATs + M2D fusion**
   - Concatenate or gated-fuse:
     ```text
     [M2D attentive embedding, BEATs embedding] -&gt; MLP -&gt; ArcFace / CE head
     ```

2. **Second option: ATST / ATST-F**

3. **AST**

I would not replace M2D immediately. I would add a new class, e.g.

```text
M2DPretrainedFusionClassifier
```

with config options:

```yaml
aux_model: beats   # beats | ast | atst
fusion_mode: concat_mlp
freeze_aux: true
m2d_embedding_dim: 512
aux_embedding_dim: ...
```

Then train it on:

1. clean dry sources, stage 1/2
2. cached USS/TSE estimated sources, stage 3

That gives a stronger classifier while preserving the current S5 pipeline and allowing clean ablations against `M2DSingleClassifierStrong`.

Also, I completed the previous remaining-work item: added `src/evaluation/export_sc_finetune_cache.py` and documented it in `recipes.md`, so we now have a concrete path to fine-tune SC on cached estimated sources. 019db5e7-f91d-7200-8dc8-9f047e8df20c" open><summary style="border:1px solid #d7eadf;border-left:8px solid #3fa56b;background:#f5fcf7;border-radius:18px;padding:22px 24px;margin:14px 0 22px 0;box-shadow:0 6px 18px rgba(63,165,107,0.08);padding-bottom:14px;"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;"><span style="font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;padding:4px 10px;border-radius:999px;background:#dff5e7;color:#1c6b41;">ASSISTANT</span><span style="font-size:26px;font-weight:800;color:#172033;">44. <meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-user-47-2026-04-24-00-57-45-cst" data-role="user" data-label="47. User" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-user-47-2026-04-24-00-57-45-cst" class="message-card" data-role="user" data-search="User Please finish your recommendation for using pretrained models for classification:

Best first upgrade: BEATs + M2D fusion

Keep M2DSingleClassifierStrong.
Add frozen BEATs embeddings.
Concatenate or gated-fuse:
[M2D attentive embedding, BEATs embedding] -&gt; MLP -&gt; ArcFace / CE head
BEATs is strong for AudioSet-like event semantics and should help noisy separated sources.
Second option: ATST / ATST-F

Very attractive for event detection because ATST-style models preserve temporal event cues better than clip-level AST.
Useful for source estimates that contain only part of an event.
AST

Allowed and easy conceptually, but often less attractive than BEATs/ATST now unless you already have stable AST tooling/checkpoints.
I would not replace M2D immediately. I would add a new class, e.g.

M2DPretrainedFusionClassifier
with config options:

aux_model: beats   # beats | ast | atst
fusion_mode: concat_mlp
freeze_aux: true
m2d_embedding_dim: 512
aux_embedding_dim: ...
Then train it on:

clean dry sources, stage 1/2
cached USS/TSE estimated sources, stage 3
That gives a stronger classifier while preserving the current S5 pipeline and allowing clean ablations against M2DSingleClassifierStrong. 019db5e7-f91d-7200-8dc8-9f047e8df20c" open><summary style="border:1px solid #dce5f3;border-left:8px solid #4f7cff;background:#f7faff;border-radius:18px;padding:22px 24px;margin:14px 0 22px 0;box-shadow:0 6px 18px rgba(79,124,255,0.08);padding-bottom:14px;"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;"><span style="font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;padding:4px 10px;border-radius:999px;background:#e2ebff;color:#234ca8;">USER</span><span style="font-size:26px;font-weight:800;color:#172033;">47. <meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-48-2026-04-24-00-57-53-cst-" data-role="assistant" data-label="48. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-48-2026-04-24-00-57-53-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant I’ll turn that recommendation into the actual baseline path now: first I’ll inspect the current classifier code/configs and dependency style, then I’ll add the fusion model and docs in a way that can still run CPU smoke tests without downloading checkpoints.

I found the repo still clean except two unrelated untracked HTML files in the parent checkout, and `main` is still one commit ahead because the previous push could not authenticate. I’m reading the classifier implementation now so the pretrained-fusion path follows the same output contract as the current S5 pipeline.

The current SC path is compact and clean: both classifiers return `embedding/logits/plain_logits/energy`, and the lightning/loss code only depends on those keys. I’m going to keep that contract and make the pretrained branch optional/frozen by default, with a clear failure message if the requested aux model backend is not installed or the checkpoint is missing.

I’m going to edit `m2d_sc.py` now. The key choice is to make the auxiliary pretrained encoder a wrapper, so BEATs/AST/ATST backends can be swapped without changing the S5 classifier contract.

The aux wrapper is in place. Next I’m adding `M2DPretrainedFusionClassifier` itself as a subclass of the strong M2D classifier, so training, validation, and S5 inference still see the same keys and prediction format.

I’ll add BEATs-fusion configs for the three SC stages: clean source ArcFace, energy/silence tuning, and estimated-source fine-tuning. The defaults assume local official BEATs code/checkpoint, so users can stay offline after setup.

I’m expanding `recipes.md` with the “how to actually pick and train it” notes now: BEATs as first fusion choice, ATST/AST alternatives, required local assets, and the exact configs/eval config to use.

The docs now have the recipe path and backend guidance. I’m going to run a tight set of checks next; because this host has no M2D/BEATs checkpoints and no `transformers` in the venv, I’ll use the existing stub strategy plus the explicit smoke-test `identity` backend for the new fusion class.

The first fusion smoke surfaced a test-stub problem rather than a model bug: my fake mel frontend produced negative “mel power,” so M2D’s log-mel step created NaNs. I’m rerunning with a positive fake mel frontend and no unnecessary resampling to test the actual fusion path.

The broad syntax/YAML checks are clean. I’m doing one more targeted smoke after the small robustness patch, including the fusion loss/predict path.

Implemented the pretrained-classification recommendation as a real baseline path.

What changed:
- Added BEATs-fusion train configs:

Validation passed:
- `git diff --check`
- full `src` Python compile

I could not instantiate real BEATs/AST/ATST on this host because the BEATs/M2D checkpoints are absent and this `.venv` does not currently have `transformers` installed. The code path is optional and gives explicit setup errors when those assets are missing.

References used: BEATs official repo, Hugging Face AST docs, and ATST-SED reference repo:
https://github.com/microsoft/unilm/tree/master/beats
https://huggingface.co/docs/transformers/model_doc/audio-spectrogram-transformer
https://github.com/Audio-WestlakeU/ATST-SED

Current repo state: these new changes are uncommitted. The branch is also still `ahead 1` from the previous local commit that could not be pushed because GitHub auth/push permission was unavailable.

<meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-50-2026-04-24-06-53-19-cst-" data-role="assistant" data-label="50. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-50-2026-04-24-06-53-19-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant I’m pulling the exact code slices so I can explain this cleanly against the real implementation, not from memory.

Sure. The short version is: I added a small wrapper class, `FrozenPretrainedAudioEncoder`, so the new fusion classifier can use different kinds of pretrained audio encoders without changing the rest of the SC pipeline. The wrapper lives in [m2d_sc.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/m2dat/m2d_sc.py:74), and the fusion classifier uses it in [M2DPretrainedFusionClassifier](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/m2dat/m2d_sc.py:619).

What each backend means:

- `official_beats`:
  This is the “use Microsoft’s original BEATs code directly” path. In [_init_official_beats](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/m2dat/m2d_sc.py:161), it imports `BEATs` and `BEATsConfig`, loads a local `.pt/.pth` checkpoint, and then in [_forward_official_beats](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/m2dat/m2d_sc.py:262) calls `extract_features(...)`. This is the path I used for the new BEATs configs because it is the most direct and stable way to use BEATs.

- `transformers`:
  This is the generic Hugging Face path. In [_init_transformers](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/m2dat/m2d_sc.py:186), it loads `AutoModel` or `AutoModelForAudioClassification`, plus `AutoFeatureExtractor` when needed. In [_forward_transformers](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/m2dat/m2d_sc.py:267), it can take either `logits`, `pooler_output`, or pooled `last_hidden_state`. This makes AST easy, and it also gives a clean path for any ATST-like model published through HF.

- `torchscript`:
  This is the “bring your own scripted encoder” path. In [_init_torchscript](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/m2dat/m2d_sc.py:231), it loads a local TorchScript model with `torch.jit.load`. In [_forward_torchscript](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/m2dat/m2d_sc.py:297), it accepts a few common output styles: raw tensor, tuple, or dict with keys like `embedding`, `features`, or `logits`. I added this because ATST/ATST-F packaging can vary a lot, and TorchScript is a nice neutral bridge.

- `identity`:
  This is not a real pretrained model. In [_identity_embedding](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/m2dat/m2d_sc.py:251), it builds a cheap fake embedding from waveform statistics: mean, std, max, min, RMS, and zero-crossing rate. I added it only so I could run CPU smoke tests for the fusion code on a machine that does not have BEATs checkpoints or HF models installed.

A couple of useful details:

Why I did it this way: one classifier class, one output contract, multiple pretrained-model paths. So S5, the lightning module, and the ArcFace loss do not need to care whether the aux embedding came from BEATs, AST, ATST-F, TorchScript, or just a smoke-test stub. 019db5e7-f91d-7200-8dc8-9f047e8df20c" open><summary style="border:1px solid #d7eadf;border-left:8px solid #3fa56b;background:#f5fcf7;border-radius:18px;padding:22px 24px;margin:14px 0 22px 0;box-shadow:0 6px 18px rgba(63,165,107,0.08);padding-bottom:14px;"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;"><span style="font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;padding:4px 10px;border-radius:999px;background:#dff5e7;color:#1c6b41;">ASSISTANT</span><span style="font-size:26px;font-weight:800;color:#172033;">50. This is the path I used for the new BEATs configs because it is the most direct and stable way to use BEATs.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">- <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">transformers</code>:<br>  This is the generic Hugging Face path. In [_init_transformers](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/m2dat/m2d_sc.py:186), it loads <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">AutoModel</code> or <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">AutoModelForAudioClassification</code>, plus <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">AutoFeatureExtractor</code> when needed. In [_forward_transformers](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/m2dat/m2d_sc.py:267), it can take either <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">logits</code>, <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">pooler_output</code>, or pooled <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">last_hidden_state</code>. This makes AST easy, and it also gives a clean path for any ATST-like model published through HF.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">- <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">torchscript</code>:<br>  This is the “bring your own scripted encoder” path. In [_init_torchscript](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/m2dat/m2d_sc.py:231), it loads a local TorchScript model with <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">torch.jit.load</code>. In [_forward_torchscript](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/m2dat/m2d_sc.py:297), it accepts a few common output styles: raw tensor, tuple, or dict with keys like <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">embedding</code>, <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">features</code>, or <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">logits</code>. I added this because ATST/ATST-F packaging can vary a lot, and TorchScript is a nice neutral bridge.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">- <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">identity</code>:<br>  This is not a real pretrained model. In [_identity_embedding](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/m2dat/m2d_sc.py:251), it builds a cheap fake embedding from waveform statistics: mean, std, max, min, RMS, and zero-crossing rate. I added it only so I could run CPU smoke tests for the fusion code on a machine that does not have BEATs checkpoints or HF models installed.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">A couple of useful details:</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Why I did it this way: one classifier class, one output contract, multiple pretrained-model paths. So S5, the lightning module, and the ArcFace loss do not need to care whether the aux embedding came from BEATs, AST, ATST-F, TorchScript, or just a smoke-test stub.</p></div></div></details>

<meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-54-2026-04-24-07-13-20-cst-" data-role="assistant" data-label="54. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-54-2026-04-24-07-13-20-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant I’m going to ground this in the actual baseline flow first: what metadata the on-the-fly synthesizer already has, what the current datasets keep or discard, and where each stage could realistically consume temporal supervision without wrecking the existing pipeline.

I’ve confirmed something important already: the synthesizer path almost certainly already has event-time metadata available, but most of the current training wrappers either drop it or only use the zero-padded source waveform implicitly. I want one more pass over the losses/model heads before I give you a real recommendation, because that’s where “timestamps will help” turns into either a clean win or a lot of extra complexity for not much gain.

I want to verify the exact metadata shape inside SpAudSyn rather than hand-wave “it probably has onset/offset.” That will tell us whether the cleanest solution is timestamp intervals, frame activity masks, or both.

I’ve got the central shape of it now: timestamps are already latent in the synthetic pipeline, but the safe value comes from using them as supervision and then passing predicted temporal cues between stages, not from giving oracle timestamps to later stages at inference. I want one quick look at the S5 orchestration code so the plan can name the actual integration points instead of just saying “wire it later.”

I have the shape of the recommendation. I’m just grabbing line-numbered references for the exact places where timestamps already exist and where the current pipeline throws that information away, so the plan can point to concrete edit sites.

Yes, I think this is possible, and done the right way it has a real chance to help. But the important distinction is this:

You should not make later stages depend on oracle timestamps at inference time.

The right version is:

- use synthetic timestamps as supervision during training
- teach each stage to predict temporal activity
- pass those predicted temporal cues across stages at inference

That avoids train/test mismatch and keeps the solution challenge-realistic.

**What The Repo Already Has**

The good news is that most of the raw ingredients already exist.

So the baseline is already very close to supporting this. The missing piece is explicit temporal supervision and stage-to-stage temporal handoff.

**Will It Help?**

My honest read:

Why I think SC benefits most:
the classifier is currently trained on full zero-padded source waveforms, but it pools clipwise. For short events, a lot of the input is silence. Explicit activity supervision should help it focus on the active region instead of learning that only through weak global pooling.

Why USS/TSE can also benefit:
the targets already contain silence outside the event span, so the models do get an implicit temporal signal. But explicit framewise activity targets can reduce temporal bleeding, false activations, and unstable conditioning.

What timestamps will not solve:
if two same-class events happen at the same time and overlap heavily, timestamps alone do not disambiguate them. Spatial cues are still the main separator there.

**My Recommendation**

Do not start by “feeding timestamps in” as oracle inputs.

Start with a new family I’d call `Temporal-Aware S5`:
- timestamps used as training supervision
- each stage predicts activity over time
- later stages consume predicted activity, not oracle activity

That is the version most likely to improve SA-SDR without poisoning inference realism.

**Detailed Plan**

1. **Data Layer First**
- Add a temporal annotation helper that converts `event_time` and `event_duration` into:
  - `onset_sec`, `offset_sec`
  - sample mask
  - STFT-frame mask
  - M2D-frame mask
- For cached stage-3 estimated-source training, use either:
  - sidecar JSON spans, or

2. **SC First, Because It’s Highest ROI**
- Add:
  - frame activity head
  - activity-aware pooling
- In inference:
  - pool only predicted-active frames, or
  - crop to predicted active span before pooling

3. **USS Second**
- Keep current waveform loss, but add:
  - activity BCE or Dice
  - inactive-region suppression penalty

4. **TSE Third**
- Use:
  - current masked SNR
  - active-frame reconstruction term
  - inactive suppression term
  - activity BCE

5. **S5 Integration**
  - USS -&gt; SC: crop or weight source classification by predicted active region
  - SC -&gt; TSE: pass predicted activity or active-window enrollment
  - TSE -&gt; refinement: reuse refined temporal activity

6. **Ablation Order**
- baseline
- `+ temporal SC`
- `+ temporal SC + temporal USS`
- `+ temporal SC + temporal USS + temporal TSE`
- `+ stage-to-stage temporal handoff`

That order matters. I would not build the full thing in one jump.

**One More Important Point**

You do not need to abandon on-the-fly synthesis.

I would keep on-the-fly audio generation, and generate temporal masks from metadata on the fly too. If you want reproducibility across stages, use metadata manifests, not fully baked waveform dumps. The repo already has `metadata` mode for that pattern.

**My Bottom-Line Recommendation**

Yes, this is worth pursuing.

But I would scope the new solution like this:

- Phase A: temporal supervision in the data layer
- Phase B: temporal-aware SC
- Phase C: temporal USS
- Phase D: temporal TSE
- Phase E: temporal-aware S5 handoff

If you want, next I can turn this into an implementation blueprint with exact new tensors, output dict keys, loss names, config flags, and the concrete file-by-file patch plan.

<meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-56-2026-04-24-07-23-15-cst" data-role="assistant" data-label="56. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-56-2026-04-24-07-23-15-cst" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant Yes. Here’s the blueprint I’d use.

**Core Decision**

Make timestamps/spans a supervised latent signal, not an oracle runtime dependency.

The new solution should be:

`Temporal-Aware S5`
- synthetic spans available during training
- each stage predicts temporal activity

I would start on the current strongest non-fusion path first:
- `ModifiedDeFTUSSMemoryEfficient`
- `M2DSingleClassifierStrong`
- `ModifiedDeFTTSEMemoryEfficient`

After that works, port the same temporal branch to BEATs/fPaSST fusion SC.

**1. Canonical Temporal Representation**

Use spans in seconds as the canonical target. Do not store dense masks as the primary truth.

New canonical tensors:
- `span_sec`: `[S, 2]`, `float32`
  - row = `[onset_sec, offset_sec]`
- `active_mask`: `[S]`, `bool`
  - already exists for TSE, keep it

Why spans first:
- cheap
- model-agnostic

**2. How To Build Spans**

There are two sources of truth:

1. Generate / metadata mode:
- read `event_time` and `event_duration` from SpAudSyn metadata

2. Waveform / cached mode:
- derive span from zero-padded oracle `dry_sources`
- use threshold over waveform energy, not filename
- this avoids needing a sidecar manifest for stage-3 SC at first

**3. New Utility Layer**

Add a new file:

Functions:
- `resample_activity_between_clocks(src_prob, src_ts_sec, dst_ts_sec)`

This file becomes the single place for:
- metadata-to-span
- waveform-to-span
- span-to-frame-mask
- prob-to-span

**4. Exact New Dataset Keys**

**USS dataset**
Patch [uss_dataset.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/datamodules/uss_dataset.py:22)

Add:
- `foreground_span_sec`: `[Nfg, 2]`
- `interference_span_sec`: `[Nint, 2]`
- `noise_span_sec`: `[1, 2]`
- `mixture_duration_sec`: `float`

Keep existing:
- `foreground_waveform`
- `interference_waveform`
- `noise_waveform`
- `class_index`
- `is_silence`

**TSE dataset**
Patch [tse_dataset.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/datamodules/tse_dataset.py:6)

Add:
- `span_sec`: `[S, 2]`
- `mixture_duration_sec`: `float`

Keep:
- `label_vector`
- `enrollment`
- `waveform`
- `active_mask`

**SC dataset**
Patch [source_classifier_dataset.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/datamodules/source_classifier_dataset.py:5)

Add:
- `span_sec`: `[2]`
- `mixture_duration_sec`: `float`

Keep:
- `waveform`
- `class_index`
- `is_silence`

For `EstimatedSourceClassifierDataset`, derive `span_sec` from oracle `dry_sources` in waveform mode.

**5. Exact New Model Outputs**

**SC temporal strong**
In [m2d_sc.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/m2dat/m2d_sc.py)

New class:
- `M2DSingleClassifierTemporalStrong`

Later:
- `M2DPretrainedFusionTemporalClassifier`

New output keys:
- `embedding`: `[B, D]`
- `logits`: `[B, C]`
- `plain_logits`: `[B, C]`
- `energy`: `[B]`
- `frame_activity_logits`: `[B, Tm2d]`
- `frame_activity_prob`: `[B, Tm2d]`
- `frame_timestamps_sec`: `[Tm2d]`

`predict(...)` additionally returns:
- `activity_span_sec`: `[B, 2]`

Implementation idea:
- use M2D time sequence before final pooling
- add `activity_head = Linear(feature_dim, 1)`
- use predicted activity for weighted pooling

**USS temporal**
Patch [modified_deft.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/deft/modified_deft.py)

Add optional activity head to the object feature map before final mask projection.

New output keys:
- existing waveform keys unchanged
- `object_activity_logits`: `[B, Nobj, Tstft]`
- `object_activity_prob`: `[B, Nobj, Tstft]`
- `frame_timestamps_sec`: `[Tstft]`

Convenience aliases:
- `foreground_activity_prob`: `[B, Nfg, Tstft]`
- `interference_activity_prob`: `[B, Nint, Tstft]`
- `noise_activity_prob`: `[B, 1, Tstft]`

**TSE temporal**
Patch [modified_deft.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/deft/modified_deft.py) for `ModifiedDeFTTSEMemoryEfficient`

New optional input:
- `temporal_hint_sec`: `[B, S, 2]`

New outputs:
- `waveform`: `[B, S, 1, L]`
- `activity_logits`: `[B, S, Tstft]`
- `activity_prob`: `[B, S, Tstft]`
- `frame_timestamps_sec`: `[Tstft]`

At inference, S5 can convert `activity_prob -&gt; activity_span_sec`.

**6. Exact New Loss Terms**

Add a helper loss file:

Functions:
- `inactive_suppression_loss(waveform, span_sec, sample_rate, active_mask=None)`

**SC loss**
Extend [m2d_sc_arcface.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/training/loss/m2d_sc_arcface.py)

New metrics:
- `loss_arcface`
- `loss_kl`
- `loss_energy`
- `loss_activity`
- `loss`

Default:
- `loss = arcface + kl + lambda_energy * energy + lambda_activity * activity`

**USS loss**
Extend [uss_loss.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/training/loss/uss_loss.py:23)

New metrics:
- `loss_fg`
- `loss_int`
- `loss_noise`
- `loss_ce`
- `loss_kl`
- `loss_silence`
- `loss_activity_fg`
- `loss_activity_int`
- `loss_activity_noise`
- `loss_activity`
- `loss`

**TSE loss**
Extend [masked_snr.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/training/loss/masked_snr.py:4)

New metrics:
- `loss_waveform`
- `loss_activity`
- `loss_inactive_suppress`
- `loss`

Recommended first formula:
- `loss = waveform + lambda_activity * activity + lambda_inactive * inactive_suppress`

**7. Exact New Lightning Target Keys**

Patch:

New target dict fields:

USS:
- `foreground_span_sec`
- `interference_span_sec`
- `noise_span_sec`

TSE:
- `span_sec`

SC:
- `span_sec`

No old keys removed.

**8. Exact S5 Integration**

Patch:

New stage handoff:

1. `USS -&gt; SC`
- use USS `foreground_activity_prob`
- convert to `foreground_span_sec`
- either:
  - crop source waveform before SC, or
  - pass `temporal_hint_sec` to SC
- I recommend crop first

2. `SC -&gt; TSE`
- SC `predict` returns `activity_span_sec`
- pass to TSE as `temporal_hint_sec`
- optionally crop enrollment waveform by span too

3. `TSE -&gt; SC refinement`
- same pattern:
  - TSE predicts refined waveform
  - SC predicts label + `activity_span_sec`
  - next TSE refinement consumes that span

**9. Config Flags**

Dataset-level:
```yaml
temporal:
  enabled: true
  source: auto            # auto | metadata | waveform
  silence_value: -1.0
  waveform_span_eps: 1e-4
```

SC model:
```yaml
predict_activity: true
activity_pooling: weighted_attentive   # weighted_attentive | weighted_meanmax
temporal_hint_mode: crop               # none | crop | bias
activity_threshold: 0.5
```

USS/TSE model:
```yaml
predict_activity: true
temporal_hint_mode: bias               # none | bias
activity_head_kernel_size: 1
```

Loss:
```yaml
lambda_activity: 0.2
lambda_inactive: 0.05
activity_margin_sec: 0.02
```

**10. New Config Files**

I would add these first:

Later, once stable:

**11. File-By-File Patch Plan**

1. `src/temporal.py`

2. `src/datamodules/dataset.py`

3. `src/datamodules/uss_dataset.py`

4. `src/datamodules/tse_dataset.py`
- emit per-slot spans

5. `src/datamodules/source_classifier_dataset.py`
- emit per-source span
- same for `EstimatedSourceClassifierDataset`

6. `src/models/m2dat/m2d_sc.py`
- add temporal SC class
- add activity head
- add weighted temporal pooling
- later port to pretrained fusion class

7. `src/training/loss/temporal.py`
- add generic span-to-frame activity loss

8. `src/training/loss/m2d_sc_arcface.py`
- add `loss_activity`

9. `src/models/deft/modified_deft.py`
- add USS activity head
- add TSE activity head
- add optional `temporal_hint_sec`

10. `src/training/loss/uss_loss.py`
- add activity supervision terms

11. `src/training/loss/masked_snr.py`
- add activity + inactive suppression terms

12. `src/training/lightningmodule/*.py`
- pass span keys through

13. `src/models/s5/kwo2025.py`
- stage-to-stage span handoff

14. `src/models/s5/self_guided_s5.py`
- same temporal refinement loop

15. `src/evaluation/export_sc_finetune_cache.py`
- optional manifest export later, but not required for first pass

16. `recipes.md`
- document training order, ablations, and temporal configs

**12. Recommended Rollout Order**

Phase 1:
- utilities + dataset spans
- temporal SC only

Phase 2:
- temporal USS

Phase 3:
- temporal TSE

Phase 4:
- S5 temporal handoff

Phase 5:

This order is important. SC is the cheapest and highest-ROI first step.

**13. Acceptance Tests**

For each phase:
- shape smoke on CPU
- finite loss check
- YAML parse
- 1-2 batch train step
- validation step
- end-to-end S5 smoke on one batch

Specific checks:
- silence slot span is `[-1,-1]`
- same-class duplicated events keep independent spans
- span recovery from waveform cache matches zero-padded oracle source

If you want, next I can turn this blueprint into the actual patch sequence starting with Phase 1: `src/temporal.py`, dataset span plumbing, and `M2DSingleClassifierTemporalStrong`.

<details id="msg-assistant-58-2026-04-24-23-25-25-cst" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant Absolutely — here’s the current context in one place.

**Project state**

We’ve been working in `dcase2026_task4_baseline` as a stronger DCASE2026 Task4 baseline, mainly around:
- `USS`
- `TSE`
- stronger `ModifiedDeFT*` variants
- pretrained-fusion classifiers

**What has already been done**

We already added or fixed a lot of the missing baseline pieces, including:

- `validation_step_processing` for:
- `evaluation_step_processing` for:
- training-set updates to include:
  - `EARS`
  - `SemanticHearing`
- stronger `ModifiedDeFTUSS` changes:
  - final `audio_head` from `2` outputs to `3`
  - reconstruction from all mixture channels to preserve spatial info
  - stronger and memory-friendlier variants
- related `ModifiedDeFTTSE` strengthening
- stronger SC path:
  - `M2DSingleClassifierStrong`
  - fusion classifier support with pretrained auxiliary encoders
- pretrained auxiliary support added for:
  - `BEATs`
  - `fPaSST`
  - generic `transformers`
  - `torchscript`
  - `identity` backend for CPU smoke tests

**Validation/testing status**

We already did a round of fast CPU-side validation for the uncommitted work at that point, including:
- compile checks
- YAML parse checks
- classifier fusion smoke tests

**Git status**

There is already a local commit created earlier:

- `de9b262 Add memory efficient DeFT Task4 recipes`

But `git push` was blocked by GitHub auth/permission, so the branch is locally ahead and not fully pushed yet.

**Latest topic we were discussing**

Most recently, we shifted to a new idea:

**temporal-aware training using synthetic timestamps/span information**

Your idea was:
- mixtures are synthesized on the fly
- then use temporal information through multiple stages:
  - `USS`
  - `Classification`
  - `TSE`

I analyzed that idea and the repo structure in detail.

**Main conclusion from that analysis**

Yes, it is feasible and promising, but the best version is:

- use timestamps as **training supervision**
- teach each stage to **predict activity over time**
- pass **predicted temporal cues** between stages at inference

So we should avoid relying on oracle timestamps at test time.

**Blueprint already prepared**

I already turned that into a detailed implementation blueprint covering:

- canonical temporal tensors like:
  - `span_sec`
  - `active_mask`
- a proposed new utility module:
- exact new dataset keys for:
  - `USSDataset`
  - `TSEDataset`
  - `SourceClassifierDataset`
- exact new model outputs for:
  - temporal SC
  - temporal USS
  - temporal TSE
- exact loss terms to add
- config flags
- stage-to-stage temporal handoff in `S5`
- file-by-file patch plan
- rollout order:
  1. temporal utilities + dataset spans + temporal SC
  2. temporal USS
  3. temporal TSE
  4. temporal-aware S5 handoff
  5. port to BEATs/fPaSST fusion SC

**Most important current status**

That temporal-aware design has been **analyzed and specified**, but it has **not yet been implemented** in code in the repo.

So the current situation is:

- the temporal-aware next-generation solution is now at the **blueprint stage**
- the logical next step is to start **Phase 1 implementation**

**Best next step**

I’d recommend we start with:

- dataset span plumbing
- `M2DSingleClassifierTemporalStrong`

That gives us the highest-ROI first slice and a clean base for the later USS/TSE temporal upgrades.

stages:<br>  - <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">TSE</code></p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">I analyzed that idea and <meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-62-2026-04-24-23-36-55-cst-" data-role="assistant" data-label="62. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-62-2026-04-24-23-36-55-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant Thanks, yes — I’ll switch the probes to `./.venv/bin/python`. I also have one earlier file-search session that may still be lingering from the interrupted turn, so I’ll cleanly check that first and then rerun the loss checks inside the repo venv.

The old search is not actually running anymore, good. The venv check is still importing, which is normal for a PyTorch environment cold start; I’ll poll it and then use that exact interpreter for the loss behavior probes.

The paper text lines up with the baseline code: the key insight is not just “use PIT”, it is “only allow PIT among outputs with the same class label.” I’m running small venv-backed probes now to check how our current losses behave for all-silence and padded-source cases.

The quick probes show two important behaviors: current TSE loss gives zero gradient when every target slot is inactive, while current USS still drives foreground waveforms even when all foreground slots are silence. I’m waiting on the CAPI probe now because importing `torchmetrics` is a little slower.

I don’t need more heavy tests to see the direction now. I’m grabbing exact line references for the losses/configs so the solution notes point to the actual places we’ll change, not vague module names.

Yes, you were right about using the repo venv. I switched to `./.venv/bin/python`; it has `torch 2.11.0+cu130`.

**Review Result**

The previous changes are directionally good for Task4 2026, especially the stronger spatial USS/TSE heads and per-source SC that can output duplicate labels. But the loss design is not yet fully aligned with the 2026 rules.

The core issue is this:

The current code only partially handles that.

**Main Findings**

1. `class_aware_pit.py` has the right paper idea, but it is incomplete for no-target mixtures.

In [class_aware_pit.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/training/loss/class_aware_pit.py:32), silence is detected from all-zero labels. Then [line 36](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/training/loss/class_aware_pit.py:36) assigns silent diagonal pairs a score of `0`.

That means an all-silence target gives constant zero loss and no waveform gradient. I verified this in the venv:

```text
all_silence_loss 0.0
all_silence_requires_grad False
```

So this loss cannot teach the separator to suppress output when no target exists.

2. `masked_snr.py` is not safe for zero-target TSE training.

[TSE masked SNR](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/training/loss/masked_snr.py:4) multiplies by `active_mask` and divides by `active_mask.sum().clamp_min(1.0)`. For all inactive slots, the loss is `-0.0` and gradient is zero. I verified:

```text
masked_snr_all_inactive_loss -0.0
pred_grad_abs_sum 0.0
```

So zero-label TSE queries are not trained to output silence.

3. `masked_snr.py` also does not solve duplicate same-class query ambiguity.

For TSE/LQSS, duplicated label queries are ambiguous. The paper’s fix is class-aware PIT: only permute outputs among queries with the same label. Current [masked_snr.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/training/loss/masked_snr.py:16) still assumes slot-aligned targets.

4. `uss_loss.py` is not order-invariant for foreground sources.

[uss_loss.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/training/loss/uss_loss.py:33) computes foreground SA-SDR slot-by-slot. But USS outputs are unconditioned slots, so the order is arbitrary. This is fragile for all mixtures and especially duplicated same-class mixtures.

For all-silence foreground targets, I saw:

```text
uss_all_silence_loss 94.7818603515625
foreground_grad_abs_sum 7.043859958648682
```

That does push toward zero, but through an SDR formula with zero targets. I would replace that with explicit inactive-energy suppression, not zero-target SDR.

5. Configs train SC on zero-target mixtures, but not USS/TSE.

SC configs already use `nevent_range: [0, 3]`, for example [m2d_sc_stage2_strong.yaml](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/config/label/m2d_sc_stage2_strong.yaml:44).

But the current stronger USS/TSE configs still use `nevent_range: [1, 3]`, for example:

So the classifier sees zero-target cases, but separation models mostly do not.

**Paper-Aligned Interpretation**

The paper’s key point is not generic PIT. It is constrained PIT:

The current metric implementation follows that spirit: [s5capi_metric.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/evaluation/metrics/s5capi_metric.py:101) excludes silence labels, and [lines 134-137](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/evaluation/metrics/s5capi_metric.py:134) assign zero-valued penalties for false negatives or false positives.

**Clear Solution**

I would make the solution loss-first:

1. Replace `masked_snr.py` with a new CA-PI TSE loss.

For TSE, use class-aware PIT over active non-silence queries:

```text
loss_tse =
  loss_capi_sdr_active
  + lambda_inactive * inactive_output_energy
  + lambda_no_target * no_target_output_energy
```

Behavior:

2. Refactor `class_aware_pit.py` into a reusable safe implementation.

Add:
- active-only normalization, not fixed `S` averaging
- grouped same-class permutations instead of full `S!` when possible
- all-silence differentiable path
- returned `best_perm` for debugging

3. Change USS loss to source-slot PIT, not class-aware query PIT.

USS is not label-queried; it outputs unconditioned foreground slots. So for USS, the right matching is full PIT across active foreground targets with a composite cost:

```text
pair_cost =
  waveform_sa_sdr_cost
  + lambda_class * class_ce_cost
```

Then:
- matched active slots get waveform + class CE
- no-target mixtures train all foreground slots to silence

4. Keep the current SC direction, but calibrate silence/count better.

`M2DSingleClassifierStrong` and the BEATs/fPaSST fusion path are compatible with duplicate labels because they classify each separated source independently. The missing part is better threshold/count calibration:
- tune energy thresholds with CAPI-SDRi, not only source accuracy
- include zero-target and near-silent estimated sources in stage-3 SC fine-tuning
- never enforce unique labels in S5 inference

5. Update training configs after the loss fix.

Once the losses are safe, change USS/TSE configs to include zero-target cases:

```yaml
nevent_range: [0, 3]
```

I would also add an explicit config knob later:

```yaml
zero_target_rate: 0.1
```

That is cleaner than relying only on uniform random event count.

6. Update S5 inference for no-target behavior.

In [kwo2025.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/s5/kwo2025.py:54), SC already can return all-zero labels. We should add:
- if all SC labels are silence, skip TSE refinement or force zero query outputs
- keep duplicate predicted labels

**Recommended Patch Order**

1. Add safe CA-PI helpers in `src/training/loss/class_aware_pit.py`.
2. Replace TSE loss with CA-PI + inactive suppression.
3. Replace USS foreground loss with PIT matching + inactive suppression.
4. Set USS/TSE `nevent_range: [0, 3]`.
5. Add CPU smoke tests:
   - duplicate same-class target swap gives low loss
   - distinct labels cannot swap
   - all-silence target has nonzero gradient to output waveform
   - S5 can return all silence without hallucinated labels
6. Document the new 2026 loss recipe in `recipes.md`.

No file edits were made in this turn. This was the review and solution design pass.

<meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-user-63-2026-04-24-23-46-13-cst" data-role="user" data-label="63. User" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-user-63-2026-04-24-23-46-13-cst" class="message-card" data-role="user" data-search="User For the interferece signals, should it apply the CA-PIT loss? 019db5e7-f91d-7200-8dc8-9f047e8df20c" open><summary style="border:1px solid #dce5f3;border-left:8px solid #4f7cff;background:#f7faff;border-radius:18px;padding:22px 24px;margin:14px 0 22px 0;box-shadow:0 6px 18px rgba(79,124,255,0.08);padding-bottom:14px;"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;"><span style="font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;padding:4px 10px;border-radius:999px;background:#e2ebff;color:#234ca8;">USER</span><span style="font-size:26px;font-weight:800;color:#172033;">63. <meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-64-2026-04-24-23-46-24-cst" data-role="assistant" data-label="64. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-64-2026-04-24-23-46-24-cst" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant Usually: **no, not class-aware PIT for interference**.

For this Task4 setup, CA-PIT is mainly needed when the model is extracting or separating **target sources with semantic labels**, because duplicated target labels create an alignment ambiguity:

```text
target query labels: [Speech, Speech, Dog]
outputs:             [slot0,  slot1,  slot2]
references:          [spkA,   spkB,   dog]
```

The two `Speech` outputs can be swapped, so CA-PIT is the right constraint.

For **interference signals**, there normally is no evaluated semantic label list and no downstream CAPI-SDRi matching by interference class. In our USS design, interference is more like an auxiliary residual/non-target bucket. So I would use:

- **full PIT** across interference slots if there are multiple interference references
- **energy suppression** for padded inactive interference slots
- optionally **residual consistency** with mixture energy, but carefully weighted

So the interference loss should be closer to:

```text
loss_interference =
  pit_sdr_loss(interference_est, interference_ref, active_interference_mask)
  + lambda_inactive_int * inactive_energy(interference_est, inactive_interference_mask)
```

not CA-PIT.

The only case where CA-PIT would make sense for interference is if we explicitly start preserving interference labels/classes and want the model to separate multiple interference events by semantic class. Current baseline does not use interference that way, and the final Task4 metric does not reward interference separation directly.

For the stronger solution, I’d recommend:

- `interference sources`: ordinary PIT

That gives the right learning pressure without over-constraining an auxiliary branch. 019db5e7-f91d-7200-8dc8-9f047e8df20c" open><summary style="border:1px solid #d7eadf;border-left:8px solid #3fa56b;background:#f5fcf7;border-radius:18px;padding:22px 24px;margin:14px 0 22px 0;box-shadow:0 6px 18px rgba(63,165,107,0.08);padding-bottom:14px;"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;"><span style="font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;padding:4px 10px;border-radius:999px;background:#dff5e7;color:#1c6b41;">ASSISTANT</span><span style="font-size:26px;font-weight:800;color:#172033;">64. Assistant</span><span class="summary-chevron">&#8250;</span></div></summary><div style="border:1px solid #d7eadf;border-left:8px solid #3fa56b;background:#f5fcf7;border-radius:18px;padding:22px
