<meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-66-2026-04-24-23-54-19-cst-" data-role="assistant" data-label="66. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-66-2026-04-24-23-54-19-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant Let’s turn the review into the actual stronger loss path. I’ll keep this scoped to the loss/config/docs surface, preserve the existing model output contracts, and use the repo `.venv` for CPU smoke tests so we’re testing the real environment this time.

I’m going to make the loss helpers reusable first, then wire TSE and USS onto them. The main compatibility choice is to keep the existing output keys (`waveform`, `foreground_waveform`, `class_logits`, etc.) so models, Lightning modules, and evaluation configs do not need a structural rewrite.

I’m editing the losses now. The key change is that “inactive” is no longer a zero-loss corner case: inactive target slots will explicitly penalize output energy, while active duplicated same-class queries still use class-aware PIT.

I also added an inference guard in `Kwon2025S5`: when the source classifier says a sample has no target labels, the S5 chain now returns silent outputs for that sample instead of letting TSE refinement create something that could be reclassified as a target. Next I’m updating the training configs to actually include zero-target mixtures.

I’m adding a small standalone smoke test file rather than depending on a test framework. It will be runnable with `./.venv/bin/python tests/test_task4_2026_losses.py` and covers exactly the four failure modes we discussed.

The first implementation slice is in place. I’m running the new smoke tests now; if anything shakes loose, I’ll patch it directly rather than leaving you with a brittle recipe.

The test itself found a packaging assumption: when run as a file under `tests/`, Python does not automatically put the repo root on `sys.path`. I’m making the smoke test self-contained so it runs exactly as documented.

Good, the requested smoke tests pass. I’m doing one more practical pass over the USS/TSE loss entry points with realistic dict keys, because the helper tests are useful but the training pipeline calls the `get_loss_func()` surfaces.

The loss entry-point checks are healthy: USS, TSE, and the generic CAPI loss all produce finite losses and nonzero gradients in the inactive/no-target paths. I’m updating `recipes.md` now so the new behavior is visible to whoever trains from the configs later.

Docs are updated with the new training recipe and the exact smoke-test command. I’m doing the broader validation pass now: compile, YAML parse, diff whitespace, and the focused smoke tests again.

The broad checks are clean so far: no whitespace issues, all source files compile, YAML parses, and the new smoke tests pass. I’m reviewing the final diff now for any accidental overreach or naming mismatch before I wrap this up.

I made the config knobs explicit and tightened a couple of scalar tensor checks for GPU safety. I’m rerunning the validation set after those final adjustments.

Implemented the stronger Task4 2026 loss solution.

What changed:
  - same-class-only CA-PIT
  - ordinary PIT
  - inactive-slot energy suppression
  - unmatched prediction masking
  - CA-PIT for active label queries
  - foreground full PIT with waveform + class matching cost
  - interference full PIT, not CA-PIT
- Updated Lightning target plumbing:
  - if SC predicts no target labels for a sample, S5 now returns silent outputs instead of letting TSE hallucinate targets
- Added explicit loss args to the separation configs

- `git diff --check`
- full `src` Python compile
- configured loss initialization for all updated separation configs

- duplicated same-class targets can swap
- distinct labels cannot swap
- all-silence TSE target gives nonzero waveform gradient
- all-silence S5 path returns silence and skips TSE

I did not commit these changes. The repo still also contains the previous uncommitted pretrained-fusion SC changes and the unrelated untracked chat HTML files.

It will be runnable with <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">./.venv/bin/python tests/test_task4_2026_losses.py</code> and covers exactly the four failure modes we discussed.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">The first implementation slice is in place. I’m running the new smoke tests now; if anything shakes loose, I’ll patch it directly rather than leaving you with a brittle recipe.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">The test itself found a packaging assumption: when run as a file under <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">tests/</code>, Python does not automatically put the repo root on <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">sys.path</code>. I’m making the smoke test self-contained so it runs exactly as documented.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Good, the requested smoke tests pass. I’m doing one more practical pass over the USS/TSE loss entry points with realistic dict keys, because the helper tests are useful but the training pipeline calls the <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">get_loss_func()</code> surfaces.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">The loss entry-point checks are healthy: USS, TSE, and the generic CAPI loss all produce finite losses and nonzero gradients in the inactive/no-target paths. I’m updating <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">recipes.md</code> now so the new behavior is visible to whoever trains from the configs later.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Docs are updated with the new training recipe and the exact smoke-test command. I’m doing the broader validation pass now: compile, YAML parse, diff whitespace, and the focused smoke tests again.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">The broad checks are clean so far: no whitespace issues, all source files compile, YAML parses, and the new smoke tests pass. I’m reviewing the final diff now for any accidental overreach or naming mismatch before I wrap this up.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">I made the config knobs explicit and tightened a couple of scalar tensor checks for GPU safety. I’m rerunning the validation set after those final adjustments.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Implemented the stronger Task4 2026 loss solution.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">What changed:<br>  - same-class-only CA-PIT<br>  - ordinary PIT<br>  - inactive-slot energy suppression<br>  - unmatched prediction masking<br>  - CA-PIT for active label queries<br>  - foreground full PIT with waveform + class matching cost<br>  - interference full PIT, not CA-PIT<br>- Updated Lightning target plumbing:<br>  - if SC predicts no target labels for a sample, S5 now returns silent outputs instead of letting TSE hallucinate targets<br>- Added explicit loss args to the separation configs</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Validation passed with <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">./.venv</code>:<br>- <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">git diff --check</code><br>- full <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">src</code> Python compile<br>- configured loss initialization for all updated separation configs</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">The smoke tests cover:<br>- duplicated same-class targets can swap<br>- distinct labels cannot swap<br>- all-silence TSE target gives nonzero waveform gradient<br>- all-silence S5 path returns silence and skips TSE</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">I did not commit these changes.
